href="members/kgp.1167394/" class="username" dir="auto" itemprop="name">kgp</a><!-- slot: message_user_info_text --></h3><div class="extraUserInfo"><dl class="pairsJustified"><dt>Joined:</dt><dd>May 30, 2014</dd></dl><dl class="pairsJustified"><dt>Messages:</dt><dd><a href="search/member?user_id=1167394" class="concealed" rel="nofollow">2,499</a></dd></dl><dl class="pairsJustified userField_mobo"><dt>Mobo:</dt><dd>Asus Prime X299 Deluxe, Asus X99-A II</dd></dl><dl class="pairsJustified userField_cpu"><dt>CPU:</dt><dd>Intel i9-7980XE, Intel I7-6950X</dd></dl><dl class="pairsJustified userField_graphics"><dt>Graphics:</dt><dd>AORUS GTX 1080 TI-X WB, AORUS GTX 1080 TI-X</dd></dl><dl class="pairsJustified userField_mac"><dt>Mac:</dt><dd style="color:#fff;font-size:1px;"><img src="images/icons/profile/imac.png" alt="iMac" title="iMac" class="customProfileIcon">, <img src="images/icons/profile/macbook_pro.png" alt="MacBook Pro" title="MacBook Pro" class="customProfileIcon">, <img src="images/icons/profile/mac_mini.png" alt="Mac mini" title="Mac mini" class="customProfileIcon"></dd></dl><dl class="pairsJustified userField_mobile_phone"><dt>Mobile Phone:</dt><dd style="color:#fff;font-size:1px;"><img src="images/icons/profile/ios.png" alt="iOS" title="iOS" class="customProfileIcon"></dd></dl></div></div></div></div><div class="messageContent"><article><blockquote class="messageText SelectQuoteContainer ugc baseHtml"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cover-nice-small-png.303228/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cover-nice-small-png.303228/" alt="cover-nice-small.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
Up and successfully running Skylake-X/X299 with macOS High Sierra 10.13.2 !<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/imacpro-overview-png.303229/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/imacpro-overview-png.303229/" alt="iMacPro-Overview.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
This originating post constitutes a new macOS 10.13 High Sierra Desktop Guide for Skylake-X/X299, which certainly can still grow and improve by your estimated user feedback. This Skylake-X/X299 10.13 High Sierra Desktop Guide bases on the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe (although initially, tests also have been performed with the Gigabyte X299 Aorus Gaming 9, thus this latter mainboard is also partly addressed in my guide below). However, also other X299 ASUS mainboard models or X299 mainboards of other brands should be compatible with this guide by considering a few mandatory modifications detailed below. The i7-7800X (6-core) was chosen as the Skylake-X Startup Configuration Model in order to minimise the guide development costs.  It has been already replaced within the goal configuration by the i9-7980XE (18 core). All other Skylake-X models compatible with this guide are detailed in the figure below.<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/skylake-x-guide-compatibility-png.276347/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/skylake-x-guide-compatibility-png.276347/" alt="Skylake-X-Guide-Compatibility.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
Carefully consider, which Skylake-X model might be the correct choice for your specific needs. Also the note of the following limitations:<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) The i7-7640X and 7740X only support two channels DDR4-2666 and only posses 16 PCI express 3.0 lanes, which are<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">already used up by implementing a state-of-the-art 16 lane PCIe graphics adapter. Thus, there are no further PCI express 3.0 lanes for using PCIe NVMe drives or additional PCIe adapters!<br>
​</div>b.) The i7-7800X and i7-7820X already support four channels DDR4-2666 but however also possess only 28 PCI express<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">3.0 lanes! Thus by using a state-of-the-art 16 lane PCIe graphics adapter and a PCIe NVMe drive, there are nearly no PCI express 3.0 lanes remaining. When adding one or two additional PCIe adapters, one exceeds the 28 available PCI express 3.0 lanes by far! In this case, the resulting configuration might be error-prone!<br>
​</div>c.) Thus, considering a.) and b.), I strongly recommend to start at least with the i9-7900X, which already supports four<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">channels DDR4-2666 and also implements 44 PCI express 3.0 lanes​</div></div><br>
Further note, that for all Skylake-X processors, a sophisticated liquid cooling system is absolutely mandatory! For stock speeds something like the Corsair <a href="http://www.corsair.com/en-eu/hydro-series-h115i-280mm-extreme-performance-liquid-cpu-cooler" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.corsair.com%2Fen-eu%2Fhydro-series-h115i-280mm-extreme-performance-liquid-cpu-cooler&amp;hash=fd5ace96b27ab547ec2e7251785ce627" rel="nofollow">H115i</a> might by sufficient. However, if somebody aims at OverClocking (OC) of the i9-7900X or Skylake-X Processors above, sophisticated Water Blocks for CPU and VRM of e.g. <a href="https://www.ekwb.com/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ekwb.com%2F&amp;hash=f9fa02ba7db580b46a0ed88c5a61383c" rel="nofollow">EKWB</a> seem absolutely mandatory and unavoidable.<br><br>
My Skylake-X/X299 System is up, fully stable and fully functional apart from the yet non-functional onboard WLAN (WIFI) module (chipset not natively supported by OS X). For Wifi, I therefore use the <a href="http://www.osxwifi.com/apple-broadcom-bcm94360cd-802-11-a-b-g-n-ac-bluetooth-4-0-with-adapter-for-pc-hackintosh" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.osxwifi.com%2Fapple-broadcom-bcm94360cd-802-11-a-b-g-n-ac-bluetooth-4-0-with-adapter-for-pc-hackintosh&amp;hash=71dd6e12a3f701fbdb1b976d4eae7bfa" rel="nofollow">OSX WIFI PCIe Adapter</a> instead.<br><br>
Thanks to a very recent iMac Pro dump performed by <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/1401507/" class="" target="_blank">@TheOfficialGypsy</a>, we have been able to successfully implement the necessary iMacPro1,1 details in both Clover_v2.4k_r4369 (thanks to Sherlocks) and Clover Configurator v4.60.0.0 (SMBIOS details, thanks to Mackie100) by beginning of January 2018. Adding BoardID Mac-7BA5B2D9E42DDD94 under SupportedBoardIds and  iMacPro1,1 under SupportedModelProperties in /System/Library/CoreServices/PlatformSupport.plist finally allows the successful iMac Pro system boot with SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 (thanks for the hint provided by user Griven from the German Hackintosh-Forum). In addition, I just modified also Pike Alpha's ssdtPRgen.sh to be compatible with the new iMac Pro BoardID Mac-7BA5B2D9E42DDD94. ssdtPRgen.sh now also successfully generates the ssdt.aml still necessary to successfully run Xnu CPU Power Management (XCPM) for Skylake-X (see Section E.1). Both, modified <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/platformsupport-plist-zip.303116/?temp_hash=c9606d566f7ffab6bceb34a4a462240a" class="internalLink">PlatformSupport.plist</a> and modified <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssdtprgen-sh-imacpro-zip.303117/?temp_hash=c9606d566f7ffab6bceb34a4a462240a" class="internalLink">ssdtPRGen iMac Pro Source Distribution</a> are attached at the bottom of this originating post/guide.<br><br><span style="color: #ff0000">Note that formerly I used the SMBIOS iMAC 17,1 system definition, which however is still mandatory to successfully install or update our macOS High Sierra systems, as the 10.13.2 MacOS Installer package has neither the iMacPro BoardID nor iMacPro Model Properties implemented in the respective PlatformSupport.plists. A modification of the macOS Installer package unfortunately is at odd with the actual board rules.<br><br>
You therefore find two EFI-Folder distributions attached at the bottom of this guide, which are identical apart from different SMBIOS definitions: <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> for macOS High Sierra Install and Upgrade purposes in Section D.), and <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> for the final iMac Pro SMBIOS implementation at the beginning of the macOS post-installation process in Section E.) </span><br><br>
Formerly, the SMBIOS iMAC 17,1 imposed a dead end at the XHC USB side, as there was no iMac 17,1 identity neither in Apple's IOUSBHostFamily.kext nor in Apple's AppleUSBXHCIPCI.kext, which further implied the sudden dead of USBInjectAll.kext or any derivatives (e.g. X99_Injector USB 3.kext or, XHCI-200-series-injector.kext, etc.). A sophisticated XHC USB kext workaround for SMBIOS iMac17,1 however provided full XHC USB 2.0 and USB 3.0 functionality at least for the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe. This sophisticated XHC USB Kext workaround is still detailed in Section E.4), as it might be yet still required for other mainboards, e.g. X99, Series-9 mainboards.<br><span style="color: #000000"><br>
Since 10.13 SU and with AppleIntelPCHPMC, Apple now natively implements IOPCIPrimaryMatchID "a2af8068" and AppleUSBXHCISPT. Thus, with both SMBIOS iMac17,1 and  SMBIOS iMacPro1,1, all external and internal XHC USB 3.0 (USB 3.1 Gen 1 Type-A) and USB 2.0 (USB 2.0 Gen 1 Type-A) ports work natively at expected data transfer rates (90 Mb/S (USB 3.0)and 40 MB/s (USB 2.0), respectively) for all X299 mainboards. The former sophisticated XHC USB Kext Workaround is obsolete and my guide implements fully XHC compatibly with all X299 mainboards! The only remaining drawback seems to consist in the current non-functionality of USB3.0 devices in USB2.0 ports.</span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">All external and internal USB 3.1 (USB 3.1 Gen 2 Type-A and Type-C) ports were natively implemented already before on different controllers than XHC and also work at data rates up to 140 MB/s. See Section E.4 of my guide.</span><br><br>
Also the ASUS Thunderbolt EX3 Extension Card is now successfully implemented, and external Thunderbolt drives connected via Apples Thunderbolt 3 to Thunderbolt 2 Adapter work at data rates and speeds similar to those of all USB 3.1 Gen 2 Type-A and Type-C connectors, i.e. 140 MB/s and above (see Section E.5 of my guide)!<br><br><span style="color: #000000">Note that opposite to my previous EFI-Folder distributions, <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> and <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> do not contain any default audio configuration. You have to implement the audio approach of your choice during the Post Installation process in Section E.)! You can select between three possible audio implementations detailed in section E.3): 1.) The AppleALC audio approach (section E.3.1) bases on <a href="https://github.com/vit9696/AppleALC/releases" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fvit9696%2FAppleALC%2Freleases&amp;hash=929c51c3f85c2fc068e8fe0b58ab1f0d" rel="nofollow">AppleALC.kext v1.2.1</a> and <a href="https://github.com/vit9696/Lilu/releases" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fvit9696%2FLilu%2Freleases&amp;hash=e81c6ef8460113bb770f1e669cb7c492" rel="nofollow">Lilu.kext v1.2.1</a> and could be implemented thanks to the extensive efforts and brilliant work of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/933653/" class="" target="_blank">@vit9696</a> and <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/190386/" class="" target="_blank">@apfelnico</a> . 2.) The VoodooHDA audio approach (section E.3.2) bases on the <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/voodoohda/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fsourceforge.net%2Fprojects%2Fvoodoohda%2F&amp;hash=f164439eac214a5c30963f976b80d1c6" rel="nofollow">VoodooHDA.kext v2.9.0d10</a> and <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/voodoohda/files/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fsourceforge.net%2Fprojects%2Fvoodoohda%2Ffiles%2F&amp;hash=7e1e9823d975b928b1471c8e528d08d2" rel="nofollow">VoodooHDA.prefPane v1.2</a> and provides both analogue audio output/input and HDMI/DP digital audio output. 3.) Finally, <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/2393/" class="" target="_blank">@toleda</a> 's cloverALC audio approach (section E.3.3) bases on the <a href="https://github.com/toleda/audio_CloverALC/blob/master/realtekALC.kext.zip" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Ftoleda%2Faudio_CloverALC%2Fblob%2Fmaster%2FrealtekALC.kext.zip&amp;hash=8ca06b18a082b435ddb6c234ec254ac6" rel="nofollow">realtekALC.kext v2.8</a> and on an additional pathing of the native vanilla AppleHDA.kext in the /S/L/E/ directory of the System Disk and has been successfully implemented thanks to the instructions and help of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/1013009/" class="" target="_blank">@Ramalama</a>. </span><br><br>
The ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe on-board Bluetooth is natively supported and also Bluetooth Audio works OoB, however due to the non-functionality of the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe on-board Wifi Module, I also use the Bluetooth 4.0 module of the <a href="http://www.osxwifi.com/apple-broadcom-bcm94360cd-802-11-a-b-g-n-ac-bluetooth-4-0-with-adapter-for-pc-hackintosh" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.osxwifi.com%2Fapple-broadcom-bcm94360cd-802-11-a-b-g-n-ac-bluetooth-4-0-with-adapter-for-pc-hackintosh&amp;hash=71dd6e12a3f701fbdb1b976d4eae7bfa" rel="nofollow">OSX WIFI PCIe Adapter</a>, which in line with its natively supported Wifi-module also provides native Airdrop, native Handoff and native Continuity as well as keyboard support in BIOS/UEFI and Clover Boot Loader.<br><br>
Thanks to the <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/smalltree-intel-211-at-pcie-gbe-kext-zip.289090/?temp_hash=e5025470ac2a1f751e68a57b915e50c5" class="internalLink">SmallTree-Intel-211-AT-PCIe-GBE.kext</a>, also the Intel I211_AT Gigabit on-board LAN controller of the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe is now correctly implemented and fully functional, in addition to the anyway natively implemented and of course also fully operational Intel I219-V Gigabyte on-board LAN controller of the Asus Prime X299 Deluxe (see Section E.8 of my guide).<br><br>
By the way, excellent news for all ASUS freaks! Thanks to the ASUS specific  "Sync all Cores"" BIOS-function, one apparently achieves brilliant and absolute top-end Xnu CPU Power Management (XCPM) performance, as you will see below in section E.1 of my guide. In my personal opinion, the ASUS X299 Prime Deluxe is currently definitely the better choice with respect to the overall XCPM performance, at least when compared with the Gigabyte X299 Aorus Gaming 9, which actually seems to miss the ASUS-specific "Sync All Cores" BIOS-functionality and therefore hardly competes with the smooth and well settled CPU idle and max. load frequencies achieved with the primer mainboard. I already returned the latter mainboard quite a while ago. The same drawback might apply by the way also for all other non-ASUS X299 mainboards of all other different brands than ASUS.<br><br>
Like always also many thanks to <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/1887915/" class="" target="_blank">@DSM2</a>  and <a href="http://www.insanelymac.com/forum/user/1579222-pmheart/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.insanelymac.com%2Fforum%2Fuser%2F1579222-pmheart%2F&amp;hash=131e51ffe8258a41c0b40a639b9328a7" rel="nofollow">PMheart</a> for their extremely helpful and fruitful collaboration with the initial setup!<br><br>
Note that my Skylake-X/X299 system is up, absolutely stable and fully functional also under macOS 10.12.6 Sierra! The corresponding Skylake-X/X299 macOS 10.12 Sierra Desktop Guide can be found <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/skylake-x-x299-the-ultimate-customac-pro-live-the-future-now-on-macos-10-12-sierra.229354/" class="internalLink">HERE</a>!<br><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><b><span class="size5">A.)  Hardware Overview</span></b>​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/tower-small-png.294331/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/tower-small-png.294331/" alt="Tower-small.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><a alt="build.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><ul><li><b>Mainboard:</b><a href="https://www.asus.com/us/Motherboards/PRIME-X299-DELUXE/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.asus.com%2Fus%2FMotherboards%2FPRIME-X299-DELUXE%2F&amp;hash=c24f79cb059c7390fec0162bef1f6711" rel="nofollow">Asus Prime X299 Deluxe</a></li></ul><ul><li><b>CPU:</b><a href="https://www.intel.com/content/www/us/en/products/processors/core/x-series/i9-7980xe.html" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" rel="nofollow">i9-7980XE</a> (18 core, 4.4Ghz)</li></ul><ul><li><b>RAM Memory:</b><a href="https://gskill.com/en/product/f4-3200c14q2-128gtzsw" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" (F4-3200C14Q2-128GTZSW)</li></ul><ul><li><b>GPU:</b><a href="http://www.gigabyte.us/Graphics-Card/GV-N108TAORUSX-WB-11GD#kf" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" Waterforce WB Extreme Edition </a>11GB</li></ul><ul><li><b>System Disks:</b><a href="https://www.samsung.com/us/computing/memory-storage/solid-state-drives/ssd-960-evo-m-2-1tb-mz-v6e1t0bw/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.samsung.com%2Fus%2Fcomputing%2Fmemory-storage%2Fsolid-state-drives%2Fssd-960-evo-m-2-1tb-mz-v6e1t0bw%2F&amp;hash=f776a1c60ee9fa6bd9e50a3ff786c1ea" rel="nofollow">EVO 960 NVMe M.2 1TB</a> (system disk macOS High Sierra 10.13.2); <a href="https://www.samsung.com/us/computing/memory-storage/solid-state-drives/ssd-960-evo-m-2-1tb-mz-v6e1t0bw/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.samsung.com%2Fus%2Fcomputing%2Fmemory-storage%2Fsolid-state-drives%2Fssd-960-evo-m-2-1tb-mz-v6e1t0bw%2F&amp;hash=f776a1c60ee9fa6bd9e50a3ff786c1ea" </a></li></ul><ul><li><b>Bluetooth + Wifi:</b><a href="http://www.osxwifi.com/apple-broadcom-bcm94360cd-802-11-a-b-g-n-ac-bluetooth-4-0-with-adapter-for-pc-hackintosh" target="_blank" AC-IUSBH-M1T</a></li></ul><ul><li><b>Case:</b><a href="http://www.thermaltake.com/Chassis/Full_Tower_/Core/C_00002998/Core_X71_Tempered_Glass_Edition/design.htm" target="_blank" class="externalLink - Nickel</a><br><br>

- 3x <a href="http://www.phanteks.com/PH-PWHUB.html" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.phanteks.com%2FPH-PWHUB.html&amp;hash=3947511b9fd69a5e41659ee9bfc469f4" rel="nofollow">Phantek PMW Fan Hub (up to 12 fans or 30W power consumption)</a><br><br>
- 1x <a href="http://www.aquatuning.co.uk/water-cooling/monitoring/flow-indicator/21773/alphacool-eisfluegel-flow-indicator-black-g1/4-inner-thread-plexi" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aquatuning.co.uk%2Fwater-cooling%2Fmonitoring%2Fflow-indicator%2F21773%2Falphacool-eisfluegel-flow-indicator-black-g1%2F4-inner-thread-plexi&amp;hash=b7e5d815986a79bd42bc1cf7e19c3103" rel="nofollow">Alphacool Eisflügel Flow Indicator Black G1/4 IG<br></a><br>
- <a href="http://www.aquatuning.co.uk/water-cooling/monitoring/temperature-display/7881/temperature-sensor-g1/4-with-c/f-display?c=2780" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aquatuning.co.uk%2Fwater-cooling%2Fmonitoring%2Ftemperature-display%2F7881%2Ftemperature-sensor-g1%2F4-with-c%2Ff-display%3Fc%3D2780&amp;hash=bff7337ff9871074fdfe1edcfe528bac" rel="nofollow">1x Phobya Temperatur Sensor G1/4 + C/F Display</a><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/watercooling-main-png.294330/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/watercooling-main-png.294330/" alt="Watercooling-main.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br>
​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><b><span class="size5">B.) BIOS Configuration</span></b>​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><br>
Please find below the summary of my actual Asus X299 Prime Deluxe BIOS settings and some likely already outdated Gigabyte X299 Aorus Gaming 9 BIOS settings, which I used during my initial testing period. Any user feedback that provides more actual settings for the latter mainboard is appreciated and will be immediately implemented.<br><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span class="size4"><b>B1.) ASUS BIOS Configuration</b></span>​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><br>
Before applying the specific settings, please provide your ASUS X299 Prime Deluxe with the actual and hopefully best working BIOS firmware.<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/asus-bios-basic-png.276484/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/asus-bios-basic-png.276484/" alt="ASUS-BIOS-Basic.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div>After Updating System time and System Date, enable X.M.P for your DDR4 modules. Don't forget to enable the EZ XMP Switch previously to this step on your ASUS Mainboard! Subsequently switch form the easy to the advanced ASUS BIOS Setup mode by pressing F7.<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/asus-bios-advanced-jpg.276341/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/asus-bios-advanced-jpg.276341/" alt="ASUS-BIOS-Advanced.jpg" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
I use all optimized BIOS settings (OoB, no OC yet) despite a few changes listed in detail below:<br><br>
1.) <b>/AI Tweaker/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) ASUS MultiCore Enhancement: <span style="color: #ff0000"><b>Auto</b></span> [optional "Disabled", <b><span style="color: #ff0000">see important notification below!</span></b>]<br>
b.) AVX Instruction Core Ratio Negative Offset: "<b><span style="color: #ff0000">3</span></b>" [optional "Auto", <b><span style="color: #ff0000">see important notification below!</span></b>]<br>
c.) AVX-512 Instruction Core Ratio Negative Offset: "<span style="color: #ff0000"><b>2</b></span>" [optional "Auto", <b><span style="color: #ff0000">see important notification below!</span></b>]<br>
d.) CPU Core Ratio: <b><span style="color: #ff0000">Sync All Cores</span></b> [optional "Auto", <b><span style="color: #ff0000">see important notification below!</span></b>]<br>
e.) <b><span style="color: #ff0000">CPU SVID Support:</span></b><b><span style="color: #ff0000">Enabled</span></b><b><span style="color: #ff0000">[fundamental for proper IPG CPU power </span></b><span style="color: #ff0000"><b>consumption display]</b></span><br>
f.) DRAM Frequency: DDR4-3200MHz<br>
​</div>2.) <b>/Advanced/CPU Configuration/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Hyper Threading [ALL]: Enabled<br>
​</div>3.) <b>/Advanced/CPU Configuration/CPU Power Management Configuration/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) <b><span style="color: #ff0000">Enhanced Intel Speed Step Technology (EIST):</span></b><b><span style="color: #ff0000">Enabled [fundamental for proper IPG CPU power </span></b><span style="color: #ff0000"><b>consumption </b></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #ff0000"><b>display]</b></span>​</div>b.) Autonomous Core C-States: Enabled<br>
c.) Enhanced Halt State (C1E): Enabled<br>
d.) CPU C6 report: Enabled<br>
e.) Package C-State: C6(non retention) state<br>
f.) <b><span style="color: #ff0000">Intel SpeedShift Technology: Enabled   (smooth CPU IDLE  frequencies)</span></b><br>
g.) MFC Mode Override: OS Native<br>
​</div>4.) <b>/Advanced/Platform Misc Configuration/  </b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) PCI Express Native Power Management: Disabled<br>
b.) PCH DMI ASPM: Disabled<br>
d.) ASPM: Disabled<br>
e.) DMI Link ASPM Control: Disabled<br>
f.)  PEG - ASMP: Disabled<br>
​</div>5.) <b>/Advanced/System Agent Configuration/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Intel VT for Directed I/O (VT-d): Disabled (<span style="color: #ff0000"><b>see VT-d notification below</b></span>)<br>
​</div>6.) <b>/Boot/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Fast Boot: Disabled<br>
b.) Above 4G Decoding: <span style="color: #ff0000"><b>Off</b></span><br>
c.) Set your specific Boot Option Priorities<br>
​</div>7.) <b>/Boot/Boot Configuration</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Boot Logo Display: Full Screen<br>
b.) Boot up NumLock State: Disabled<br>
c.) Setup Mode: Advanced<br>
​</div>8.) <b>/Boot/Compatibility Support Module/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Launch CSM: Disabled​</div><br>
9.) <b>/Boot/Secure Boot/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) OS Type: Other OS<br>
​</div>With F7 and F10 you can save the modified BIOS settings.<br><br><b><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: underline">Important Notes:</span></span></b><br><br><b><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: underline">"ASUS MultiCore Enhancement":</span></span></b> When set to "Auto", MCE  allows you to maximise the overclocking performance optimised by the ASUS core ratio settings. When disabled, MCE allows to set to default core ratio settings.<br><br><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><b><span style="text-decoration: underline">"CPU Core Ratio - Sync All Cores":</span></b></span><span style="color: #000000">Tremendous increase in CPU performance</span>  can be achieved with the CPU Core Ratio set to "Sync All Cores". In case of the  i9-7980XE, the <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><b>Geekbench score difference </b></span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">is approx.</span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><b> 51.000 (disabled) </b></span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">compared to</span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><b> 58.000 (enabled)</b>! </span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">Note however, that Sync All Cores should be used only</span><span style="color: #000000">in case of the availability of an excellent and extremely sophisticated water cooling system! Otherwise, CPU Core Ratio should be set to "Auto". Further note that with CPU Core Ratio set to "Sync All Cores", the AVX Instruction Core Ratio Negative Offset must be set to "3" and the AVX-512 Instruction Core Ratio Negative Offset must be set to "2". Without the correct core ratio offsets, your system might become unstable with CPU Core Ratio set to "Sync All Cores"!</span><br><br><span style="text-decoration: underline"><span style="color: #ff0000"><b>VT-d Note:</b></span></span> For compatibility with VM or parallels, VT-d can be also ENABLED... Verify however, in this case that in your config.plist the boot flag "dart=0" is checked under Arguments in the "Boot" Section of Clover Configurator!<br><br><b><span style="color: #ff0000"><span style="text-decoration: underline">Intel(R) Power Gadget (IPG) CPU Power Consumption note:</span></span></b> for the proper display of the CPU Power Consumption in e.g. the Intel(R) Power Gadget it is absolutely mandatory to enable both <b><b>/AI Tweaker/CPU SVID Support/ </b></b>and<b><b><b>/Advanced/CPU Configuration/CPU Power Management Configuration/<b>Enhanced Intel Speed Step Technology (EIST)</b></b></b></b><br><br><b><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: underline">CPU Core Voltage Correction for ASUS X299 mainboard users:</span></span></b> The ASUS Skylake-X BIOS microcode implementation is still somewhat buggy. With "<b>/AI Tweaker/CPU Core Voltage/</b>" set to "<b>Auto</b>", the CPU Core Voltages assigned to your Skylake-X CPU might be simply too high. This actually does not only affect the OSX but also the Windows performance in the same way!<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cpu-core-voltage-auto-png.300826/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cpu-core-voltage-auto-png.300826/" alt="CPU-Core-Voltage-Auto.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
It is recommended to fix the CPU Core Voltage in the ASUS mainboard BIOS to a minimum value that still provides flawless system boot and full system performance during CPU max. load conditions in line with significantly CPU core temperatures. With CPU max. load conditions I refer to the max. turbo frequency (e.g. 4.4 Ghz for the i9-7980XE) applied to ALL cores!<br><br><span style="text-decoration: underline">The optimal CPU Core Voltage setting can be retrieved within the following iterative approach:</span><br><br>
Note that the iterative approach detailed below assumes the BIOS settings described in Section B1) - point 1) to 10) above, however by considering the following else optional settings:<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>
i.) "ASUS MultiCore Enhancement" set to "Auto"<br>
ii.) "CPU Core Ratio" set to "Sync All Cores"<br>
iii.) "AVX Instruction Core Ratio Negative Offset" set to "3"<br>
iv.) "AVX-512 Instruction Core Ratio Negative Offset" set to "2"​</div><br>
1.) Boot into Windows and launch <b>ASUS CPU-Z</b> as well as <b>Cinebench</b>.<br><br>
2.) Run Cinebench CPU benchmarks and watch the <b>Core VID values</b> in CPU-Z under CPU max.load conditions. These values will<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">usually exceed 1.2V with "<b>/AI Tweaker/CPU Core Voltage/</b>" set to "<b>Auto</b>"​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cpu-z-cinebench-png.300827/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cpu-z-cinebench-png.300827/" alt="cpu-z-cinebench.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a>
		
​</div><br>
3.) To optimise the "<b>/AI Tweaker/CPU Core Voltage/</b>"  perform the following steps:<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Enter the BIOS, go to "<b>/AI Tweaker/CPU Core Voltage/</b>" and change from "<b>Auto</b>" to "<b>Manual</b>"<br><br>
b.) Enter a slightly lower <b>CPU Core Voltage Overrride</b> (e.g. typically 0.01 V less) than originally observed with CPU-Z<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">under Cinebench CPU benchmark max.load conditions in Windows, e.g. 1.190 V in the first iteration.<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cpu-core-voltage-overrride-png.300828/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cpu-core-voltage-overrride-png.300828/" alt="CPU-Core-Voltage-Overrride.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br>
​</div>c.) Reboot into windows and check if the Cinebench CPU benchmark scores are still in the expected range by also controlling<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the respective <b>Core VID</b> values during the Cinebench CPU benchmark max. load conditions<br>
​</div>d.) Repeat b.) and c.) until either your Cinebench CPU benchmarks scores start to significantly decrease or you start facing<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">problems in booting your system. Given my personal experience with the i9-7980XE, a <b>CPU Core Voltage Override</b> of <b>1.120 V</b> might be optimal in any case if one does not perform any OverClocking! In case of OC, the optimal CPU Core Voltage can certainly also exceed 1.2 V, e.g. 1.32 V with a i9-7900X @ 5 Ghz OC (perfect and delidded sample), however a sophisticated water block circuit is absolutely mandatory in this case! Therefore, always watch also your CPU temps in addition when performing this iterative CPU Core Voltage Override Value Optimisation, which should not exceed 90 deg C under CPU max. load conditions!<br>
​</div></div><b><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: underline">Warning! </span></span></b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div>Before performing the CPU Core Voltage Override Value Optimisation Approach, save your actual BIOS settings to a USB Drive. If during the iterative approach you are not able to successfully boot your system, perform a CMOS reset and restore your BIOS settings from the USB Drive, by subsequently entering the last successful <b>CPU Core Voltage Override</b> value!<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div></div><b><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><b><span style="text-decoration: underline"><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)">Never but never enter CPU Core Voltage Overrride values larger than 1.xx V!</span></span><span style="color: #ff0000"> Too high voltages (e.g. 1.5-10 V) can severely damage your CPU! Thus, never forget about the comma after the 1!!! </span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)">Note if you perform this iterative CPU Core Voltage Override Value Optimisation Procedure, you perform it at your own risk!</span></b></span></b><br><br>
Many thanks to <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/1887915/" class="" target="_blank">@DSM2</a> for all his comments, valuable input, and proposed solutions.<br><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span class="size4"><b>B2.) - Initial Gigabyte BIOS Configuration</b></span>​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div><br>
Please note once more, that my Gigabyte BIOS settings initially used and such summarised below, might not reflect the actual optimum choice for this mainboard. Any user feedback is appreciated and welcome. In any case, before applying the specific settings listed below, please provide also your Gigabyte X299 Aorus Gaming 9 with the actual and hopefully best working BIOS firmware.<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/gigabyte-jpg.276340/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/gigabyte-jpg.276340/" alt="Gigabyte.jpg" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
1.) <b>/M.I.T/Advanced Frequency Settings/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Extreme Memory Profile: (X.M.P): Profile1<br>
​</div>2.) <b>/M.I.T/Advanced Frequency Settings/Advanced CPU Core Settings</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Active Cores Control: Manual<br>
b.) Hyper-Threading Technology: Enabled<br>
c.) Enhanced Multi-Core Performance: enabled/disabled (<span style="color: #ff0000"><b>optional; individual CPU compatibility yet to be verified</b></span>)<br>
d.) CPU Enhanced Halt (C1E): Enabled<br>
e.) C6/C7 State Support: Enabled<br>
f.) Package C State limit: C6<br>
g.) CPU EIST Function: Disabled<br>
​</div>3.) <b>/M.I.T/Advanced Memory Settings/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Extreme Memory Profile (X.M.P): Profile1<br>
​</div>4.) <b>/BIOS/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Boot Numlock State: Disabled<br>
b.) Security option: Setup<br>
c.) Full Screen Logo Show: Enbabled<br>
d.) Fast Boot: Disabled<br>
e.) CSM Support: Disabled<br>
​</div>5.) <b>/BIOS/Secure Boot/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Secure Boot Enable: Disabled​</div><br>
6.) <b>/Peripherals/USB Configuration/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) XHCI Hand-off: Enabled<br>
​</div>7.) <b>/Chipset/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) VT-d: Disabled (<span style="color: #ff0000"><b>see VT-d notification in Section ASUS BIOS settings above</b></span>)​</div><br>
8.) <b>/Save&amp; Exit/</b><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Save &amp; Exit​</div><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><b><span class="size5">C.) <span style="color: #b30000">Important General Note/Advice and Error Prevention</span></span></b>​</div></div></div></div><br>
Please note the following important General Note / Advice and Error Prevention, when setting up your Skylake-X/X299 System and implementing the latest respective macOS distribution.<br><br>
1.) Already since Clover_v2.4k_r4233 it is possible to directly use Clover's OsxAptioFixDrv-64.efi in<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">/EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/ in combination with <a href="https://nickwoodhams.com/x99-hackintosh-osxaptiofixdrv-allocaterelocblock-error-update/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fnickwoodhams.com%2Fx99-hackintosh-osxaptiofixdrv-allocaterelocblock-error-update%2F&amp;hash=43c0ccca4d6e780a6d8b1d994616eacf" rel="nofollow">nickwoodhams Test2-2016.efi </a>to obtain a fully functional and fully stable system. Earlier versions of OsxAptioFixDrv-64.efi resulted in unstable system performance and random reboots. Over the years, I therefore previously always employed nickwoodhams <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/osxaptiofix2drv-free2000-efi-zip.285578/?temp_hash=ae045da946c9821e37750b66b314486f" class="internalLink">OsxAptioFix2Drv-free2000.efi</a> workaround in /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/, which now has become totally obsolete! On Syklake-X/X299 Systems, The OsxAptioFix2Drv-free2000.efi workaround occasionally resulted in memory allocation errors at the very initial system boot with the following error message​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/error-jpg.272987/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="data/attachments/227/227896-a04a3e68a27913130969eaea5bddaad1.jpg" alt="error.jpg" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a>
			
​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">while during system operation, <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/osxaptiofix2drv-free2000-efi-zip.285578/?temp_hash=ae045da946c9821e37750b66b314486f" class="internalLink">OsxAptioFix2Drv-free2000.efi</a> also yielded a very stable and fully functional MacOS System.<br><br>
In any case, by using the recent Clover OsxAptioFixDrv-64.efi in combination with <a href="https://nickwoodhams.com/x99-hackintosh-osxaptiofixdrv-allocaterelocblock-error-update/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fnickwoodhams.com%2Fx99-hackintosh-osxaptiofixdrv-allocaterelocblock-error-update%2F&amp;hash=43c0ccca4d6e780a6d8b1d994616eacf" rel="nofollow">nickwoodhams Test2-2016.efi</a>, all memory allocation errors at system boot totally vanished!​</div><br><span style="color: #000000">2.) a.) </span><span style="color: #b30000"><b>All ATI Graphics Cards Users</b></span><span style="color: #000000"> with typical rudimentary and basic Starter ATI Graphics Cards like the ATI Radeon </span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #000000">RX </span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">560 or RX 580 should use </span><a href="https://github.com/vit9696/WhateverGreen/releases" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fvit9696%2FWhateverGreen%2Freleases&amp;hash=f72da8d38ffa6d42908841547be13f59" rel="nofollow">WhateverGreen.kext v1.1.4.</a><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"> and </span><a href="https://github.com/vit9696/Lilu/releases" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fvit9696%2FLilu%2Freleases&amp;hash=e81c6ef8460113bb770f1e669cb7c492" rel="nofollow">Lilu.kext v1.2.1</a><span style="color: #000000">. <br><br>
Not however, that all ATI Vega 64 and Frontier GPUs are natively implemented by OSX and run Out of Box (OoB). No need for the additional Whatevergreen.kext and Lilu.kext implementation.  </span><br>
​</div><span style="color: #000000">b.) </span><b><span style="color: rgb(179, 0, 0)">All Nvidia Graphics Cards</span></b><span style="color: #b30000"><b>Users</b></span><span style="color: #000000"> can now employ officially distributed Nvidia 10.13 Web Drivers for their Nvidia </span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #000000">Pascal </span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">and Maxwell graphics cards since the Final Release of macOS High Sierra 10.13! Nvidia Kepler Cards were anyway already natively implemented in the earlier beta distributions of macOS 10.13. It is obvious, that in consequence, the Web Driver Workaround based on the 10.12.6 Web Driver, used during the beta testing, is obsolete.</span><br><span style="text-decoration: underline"><br><b><span style="color: #000000">If you still use the 10.13 web driver workaround, perform all steps indicated below to uninstall the patched 10.12.6 NVIDIA Web Driver and the NVIDIA Web Driver Manager primer to the  MacOS High Sierra Update!!!!</span><br></b></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">i.) Open the NVIDIA Driver Manager in the menu bar item.<br><br>
ii.) Click on the padlock icon and enter your Administrator password.<br><br>
iii.) Click the Open Uninstaller button.<br><br>
iv.) Click Uninstall and continue with the de-installation. Reboot your system as indicated<br><br>
v.) Install the native vanilla macOS High Sierra 10.13 AppleGraphicsControl.kext with the appropriate permission in<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">/S/L/E/ by means of <a href="http://www.insanelymac.com/forum/topic/140647-latest-kext-utility-macos-sierra-super-speed-edition/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.insanelymac.com%2Fforum%2Ftopic%2F140647-latest-kext-utility-macos-sierra-super-speed-edition%2F&amp;hash=af3be765388a18375b5d4e63017e3da9" rel="nofollow">Kext Utility</a>.<br>
​</div></div><span style="text-decoration: underline"><b><span style="color: #000000">If you currently use a former officially distributed Nvidia 10.13 web driver, perform all steps indicated below to uninstall this NVIDIA Web Driver and it's NVIDIA Web Driver Manager primer to the MacOS High Sierra Update!!!</span><br></b></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #000000">To do so, just perform steps a.) to d.) above primer to the MacOS Update! <br></span>​</div><b><span style="color: #000000">If you do not remove the former Nvidia Web Drivers <b>primer to the MacOS Update, your System will be unbootable after the MacOS Update</b>!!! </span><br></b><br><span style="color: #404040">For further details and error prevention see Section E.2)</span><span style="color: rgb(64, 64, 64)">.<br></span>​</div>3.) This error prevention seems already obsolete. During former macOS 10.13 clean install/upgrade attempts one received<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the following firmware verification error notification in case of connecting additional windows drives to the System:<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/frimware-error-png.273336/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="data/attachments/228/228245-5ab8db33d95a85a5107437aa39c36884.jpg" alt="Frimware-Error.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
It was therefore mandatory to unplug any Windows NVMe, SSD or HDD drives connected  in case of a dual boot configuration...<br>
​</div>4.) In the EFI-folder of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> attached at the end of this originating post/guide,<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">one finds the <span style="color: rgb(64, 64, 64)">EmuVariableUefi-64.efi </span>in the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/-directory. Note the following very important advice and error prevention:<br><br>
a.) If present in the EFI-directory of your USB Flash Drive Installer, the following error message might occur during<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the macOS system installation/upgrade:<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/error-install-png.276338/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/error-install-png.276338/" alt="error-install.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><span style="color: #ff0000"><span style="color: #404040">Thus, please remove</span></span><span style="color: #000000">the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi from the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/-directory of your USB Flash Drive Installer! </span>​</div></div></div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px">b.)  <span style="color: #404040">Note however, that it is absolutely mandatory to have the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi implemented in the </span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #404040">/EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/-directory of the System Disk as implemented in the EFI-Folder of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> and </span><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a>, attached at the bottom of this originating post/guide.<br><br>
The reason is the following: at the end of the macOS installation/update process (icloud registration of your system) or during each boot of your system disk, you need to correctly transmit your SMBIOS credentials, like Serial Number, UUID, ROM and Board Serial Number, etc. (previously created during the SMBIOS definition process detailed below) to iCloud. On systems with iMac17,1 and iMacPro1,1 SMBIOS definitions and X299-mobo, this crucial step only can be successfully performed by means of EmuVariableUefi-64.efi! Remember, that due to  Error Prevention 4.a) above, the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi file is however omitted in the USB Flash Drive Installer's EFI partition. Thus, as once more indicated in more detail in Sections D.1/12.)  and D.2/12.) below, in the last step of the MacOS Install or Update procedure one has to boot the MacOS Installer Partition on the System Disk with the EFI-partition on the System Disk, which opposite to the EFI-directory on the USB Flash Driver Installer indeed contains the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi as configured above. If in this last step of the macOS install/update procedure, the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi is missing in the respective EFI-directory at boot, one will be able to sign into iCloud but will subsequently neither be able to use iMessage nor Facetime! This fundamental problem only can be  solved by signing out from iCloud by previously unchecking in Apple's Photos Application under "Preferences" the options "iCloud Photo Library", "My Photo Stream" and "iCloud Photo Sharing", and by subsequently repeating all necessary steps detailed in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/374452/" class="" target="_blank">@P1LGRIM</a> 's <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/an-idiots-guide-to-imessage.196827/" class="internalLink">"An iDiots's Guide To iMessage"</a> and also considering a few additional own comments and modifications detailed in D.1/4.c), D.1/4.d) and D.2/4.c) below.<br>
​</div></div>5.) Avoid any MacOS assignments in KextToPatch and KernelToPatch entries implemented in the  "Kernel and Kext Patches"<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Section of the Clover Configurator. If subsequently in my Guide you still find MatchOS assignments in respective figures or text, just ignore all likely yet persistent MatchOS assignments. In the config.plist of the EFI-Folder contained in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-su-release-161017-zip.286083/?temp_hash=b1a58480b042849c3904b4d4332ae282" class="internalLink">EFI-</a><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> and <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118-zip.304121/?temp_hash=a4ebbf9ce07742393f51b4bb49a47c69" class="internalLink"></a><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a>p, all MatchOS assignments have been definitely removed.<br>
​</div>6.) The /EFI/Clover/kexts/Other/ directory of my previously distributed EFI-Folder contained a fully functional and<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">operational XHC USB Kext (<a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/kgp-asusprimex299deluxe-usb-kext-zip.274747/" class="internalLink">KGP-ASUSPrimeX299Deluxe-USB.kext</a>) for the SMBIOS iMac17,1 system definition, which successfully implemented all XHC USB 2.0 and USB 3.0 ports available on the ASUS Prime X299. Already w<span style="color: #000000">ith MacOS High Sierra Supplemental Update (SU), Error prevention 6.) has become obsolete also for all non ASUS Prime X299 boarders. With AppleIntelPCHPMC, Apple natively implements IOPCIPrimaryMatchID "a2af8068" and AppleUSBXHCISPT with the former iMac17,1 and also now with the final iMacPro1,1 system definition.  All external and internal XHC USB 3.0 (USB 3.1 Gen 1 Type-A) and USB 2.0 (USB 2.0 Gen 1 Type-A) ports now work natively at expected data transfer rates (90 Mb/S (USB 3.0)and 40 MB/s (USB 2.0), respectively) for all X299 mainboards when using SMBIOS iMac17,1. The sophisticated XHC USB Kext Workaround is herewith obsolete, and my guide provides full and direct XHC compatible with all X299 mainboards! The only remaining drawback seems to consist in the current non-functionality of USB3.0 devices in USB2.0 ports.</span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">All external and internal USB 3.1 (USB 3.1 Gen 2 Type-A and Type-C) ports were natively implemented already before on different controllers than XHC and also work at data rates up to 140 MB/s. See Section E.4 of my guide.</span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div></div>7.) If you have the Thunderbolt EX3 PCIe extension card already successfully connected with your ASUS Prime X299<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Deluxe and properly implemented in your system, disconnect any Thunderbolt 2 drives during the macOS installation/upgrade procedure. If however the Thunderbolt EX3 PCIe extension card yet has not been properly configured and implemented in your system, remove the card for the macOS Upgrade or Clean Install procedure.<br>
​</div>8.) Note that on some systems it might be necessary to check the KernelPM Option in the "Kernel and Kext Patches<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Section" of the Clover Configurator to successfully boot the respective system. Note that in the config.plist of the EFI-Folder attached below, this option is unchecked, as it is not required in case of the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe.<br>
​</div>9.) Always check that you have the most actual apfs.efi in the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/ - directories of your USB Flash<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Drive Installer and System Disk (see D.1/4.e and D.2/4.d)!<br><br>
The actual apfs.efi can be obtained by following the respective guideline detailed below:<br><br>
a.) Download and install <a href="https://www.charlessoft.com/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.charlessoft.com%2F&amp;hash=f0ddd93a3a31d65ae4f9c930ae19b63f" rel="nofollow">Pacifist for Mac</a>.<br><br>
b.) Copy the "Install macOS High Sierra.app" to your Desktop -&gt; right-click with your mouse on the app and select<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">"Show Package Contents" -&gt; click with the mouse on "Contents" and subsequently on "Shared Support" -&gt; right-click with the mouse on "BaseSystem.dmg" and select "Open With" -&gt; select "pacifist.app".  Pacifist is now loading the  "BaseSystem.dmg" package contents.<br>
​</div>c.) Now click with the mouse on "usr" -&gt; "standalone" -&gt; "i386". After a right-click on apfs.efi, select "Extract to<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Custom Location...". Choose your Desktop as Destination. Answer the subsequent question "Extract apfs.efi ?" with "Extract". You now have the most actual version of apfs.efi on your Desktop.<br>
​</div>d.) If necessary (usually the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/ - directory of my distributed EFI-Folders already contains the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">most actual apfs.efi version), copy the actual apfs.efi to the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/ - directories of your USB Flash Drive Installer and System Disk (see D.1/4.e and D.2/4.d)!<br>
​</div></div>10.)<span style="color: #000000"> To avoid boot problems and for sleep/wake functionality (not verified yet), it is absolute mandatory to </span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #000000">have VoodooTSCSync.kext in the /EFI/CLOVER/kexts/Other/ directory of both USB Flash Drive and System Disk. <br><br>
Please note that the <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/voodootscsync-kext-zip.277142/?temp_hash=934f3d395c8a98d708e517af57ece9cf" class="internalLink">VoodooTSCSync.kext</a> attached at the end of this originating post/guide is configured for a 6-core CPU (12 threads) like the i7-7800X. To adopt the kext for Skylake-X processers with more or less cores than 6 cores, apply the following approach:<br><br>
a.) Download and unzip the <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/voodootscsync-kext-zip.277142/?temp_hash=934f3d395c8a98d708e517af57ece9cf" class="internalLink">VoodooTSCSync.kext</a> attached at the end of this originating post/guide to your desktop. <br><br>
b.) Right-click with the mouse on the VoodooTSCSync.kext file and select "Show Packet Contents".<br><br>
c.) Double-click with the mouse on /contents/ . After a right-click on the "Info.plist" file, select "Open with / Other". </span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #000000">Select the TextEdit.app and edit the "Info.plist" file. <br></span>​</div><span style="color: #000000">d.) Use the "find"-function of TextEdit.app and search for the term "IOCPUNumber"<br><br>
e.) Note that the adequate IOCPUNumber for your particular Skylake-X processor is the number of its threads -1, by </span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #000000">always keeping in mind that the number of it's threads is always 2x the number of it's cores.<br></span><br>
Thus in case of the 6 core i7-7800X, the IOCPUNumber is 11 (12 threads - 1).<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">&lt;key&gt;IOCPUNumber&lt;/key&gt;<br>
&lt;integer&gt;11&lt;/integer&gt;</div></div>By following this methodology, the correct IOCPUNumber for the 10-core i9-7900X would be (20 threads -1)<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">&lt;key&gt;IOCPUNumber&lt;/key&gt;<br>
&lt;integer&gt;19&lt;/integer&gt;</div></div>and the IOCPUNumber for the 18-core i9-7980XE would result in (36 threads -1)<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">&lt;key&gt;IOCPUNumber&lt;/key&gt;<br>
&lt;integer&gt;35&lt;/integer&gt;</div></div></div>f.) After adopting the IOCPUNumber for your particular Skylake-X processor, save the info.plist file and copy the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">modified VoodooTSCSync.kext to the /EFI/CLOVER/kexts/Other/ - directories of both USB Flash Drive Installer and System Disk (see D.1/4.f and D.2/4.e)!<br>
​</div></div></div>11.) Already during the last Beta Versions of macOS 10.13 High Sierra, Apple forced the beta users to use the new Apple file<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">system APFS in case of a Clean Install/update of MacOS High Sierra 10.13. Also within macOS High Sierra 10.13.2 this is the case.  Most APSF incompatibilities with available system related software apparently have been already removed. The actual version  of <a href="https://bombich.com/de" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fbombich.com%2Fde&amp;hash=d8a9e01954ea56bae5ec8f8a4fdc798a" rel="nofollow">Carbon Copy Cloner</a> (CCC) now supports the direct cloning of APFS system disks and hereby enables the previously missing option for APFS system backups. Until Boot-Loader Distribution Clover_v2.4k_r4210, it was also impossible to install the Clover Boot-Loader in the EFI-Partition of an APFS System Disk by means of the Clover Boot-Loader Installer Package. However, with actual <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/cloverefiboot/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fsourceforge.net%2Fprojects%2Fcloverefiboot%2F&amp;hash=d0b1ed60cc55607c749fa6c5eb1291e9" rel="nofollow">Clover Boot-Loader Distributions</a>, the Clover Boot-Loader Installation works absolutely flawless on APFS System Disks.<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div>Note however, that currently it seems to be still impossible to format an APFS-disk with HFS+ by means of Apple's disk utility.<br><br>
If you need to do format an APFS-disk with HFS+, use one of the following workarounds:<br><br>
a.) <span style="text-decoration: underline">Windows work around:</span><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">i.) Install UEFI Windows as described in E.5, 1.) to 5.). Download, install and run <a href="https://www.partitionwizard.com/free-partition-manager.html" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.partitionwizard.com%2Ffree-partition-manager.html&amp;hash=2bfd4fa9f6bb2cd0fb026687e39398b2" rel="nofollow">MiniTool Partition Wizard</a><br><br>
ii.) Delete all partitions on your APSF-Disk. Else, leave the drive unformatted.<br><br>
iii.) Back to OS X, format now the unformatted disk with HFS+ [(Mac OS Extended (Journaled)] and a GUID partition<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">table by means of Apple's Disk Utility and you are done!<br>
​</div>The dual boot system with windows might be also helpful for some of the other preparatory error prevention steps mentioned above, if you do not have any Mac or older Hackintosh available.<br>
​</div>b.) <span style="text-decoration: underline">OS X approach workaround:</span><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">In the Terminal app, type:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">diskutil list </div></div>In the output which you can read by scrolling back, you will find all internal disks named <b>/dev/disk0</b>, <b>/dev/disk1</b>, depending upon how many physical disks are present in your system.<br><br>
Making a note of the disk identifier for the disk you intend to format (you can eliminate risk by removing all but the intended target). Subsequently, you can partition and format the entire disk as HFS+ by typing the following terminal command:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">diskutil partitionDisk /dev/diskX 1 GPT jhfs+ "High Sierra" R </div></div>where <b>/dev/diskX</b> is the disk identifier mentioned above and <b>High Sierra</b> will be the label for the single partition created. The remaining <b>1 GPT jhfs+</b> and <b>R</b> arguments tell diskutil to create a single partition, within a GUID partition table, formatted as Journaled HFS+ and using the entire disk, respectively. Thanks to <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/436334/" class="" target="_blank">@dwhitla</a> for respective advices and implementations.<br><br>
Alternatively one can also use the following terminal command:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">diskutil partitionDisk /dev/diskX GPT JHFS+ New 0b</div></div>where <b>/dev/diskX</b> is again the disk identifier mentioned above and <b>NEW</b> is again the label for the disk partition created. The <b>GPT HFFS+</b> and <b>0b</b> arguments again tell diskutil to create a single partition, within a GUID partition table, formatted as Journaled HFS+ and covering the entire disk, respectively.<br>
​</div><span style="text-decoration: underline">Important additional Note:</span><br><br>
i.) Both approaches might be also useful in successfully formatting newly implemented factory pre-formatted NVME, SSD or<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">HDD drives, which cannot be directly formatted by means of Apple's disk utility.<br>
​</div>ii.) By means of the second OS X approach, brand new unformatted or not compatibly formatted system NVMe, SSD and<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">HDD system drives can be also directly formatted within the macOS Clean Install procedure.<br><br>
When presented with the initial install screen where you are presented options to <b>Restore From Backup</b> or <b>Install</b>, select <b>Terminal</b> from the <b>Utilities</b> menu bar item;<br><br>
When entering the <b>disk util </b>terminal command, there will be many virtual volumes in the output due to the installer having created temporary memory-resident disks. At the top of this output which you can read by scrolling back, you will see all internal disk(s) marked <b>(internal)</b>.<br><br>
Note however, that the previously unformatted system disk must contain the appropriate EFI-Folder in it's EFI partition for a successful macOS installation! In the final step of the macOS installation, you have to boot your system disk with the EFI-Folder of the latter! Thus, it is recommended to format and properly setup the system disk before and not during the macOS Installation!<br>
​</div>iii.) The diskutil terminal approach is also able to convert a HFS+ macOS High Sierra 10.13 System Disk to APFS.<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">To do so enter the following terminal command:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">diskutil apfs convert /dev/diskX</div></div></div></div>12.) All ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe users, who enabled the second LAN controller in the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe BIOS, are<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">advised to download, unzip and copy the <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/smalltree-intel-211-at-pcie-gbe-kext-zip.289090/" class="internalLink">SmallTree-Intel-211-AT-PCIe-GBE.kext</a> to the EFI-Folders of both USB Flash Drive Installer and 10.13 System Disk, or to disable the second LAN port in the BIOS during the MacOS Installation.<br>
​</div>13.) <span style="text-decoration: underline">Lilu and Lilu Plugin distribution remarks:</span><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Previously, I witnessed boot kernel panics (KP) on my Skylake-X/X299 system when implementing Lilu.kext v1.2.0, AppleALC.kext v1.2.0 and NvididaGraphicsFixup.kext v1.2.0 in /EFI/CLOVER/kexts/Other/ or /L/E/ (including <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/lilufriend-kext-zip.290404/?temp_hash=9cfbc1ad58ff8773d4cee16dbd0e7277" class="internalLink">LiluFriend.kext</a> in the latter directory). The KPs only could be avoided with the additional boot flag <i>-lilulowmem</i><br><br>
The Lilu KPs might have been caused by a borked kextcache. However, even a kextcache rebuild with the following terminal commands<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo touch /Library/Extensions &amp;&amp; sudo kextcache -u /<br><br>
sudo touch /System/Library/Extensions &amp;&amp; sudo kextcache -u /</div></div>did not solve the issue. KPs caused by Lilu v1.2.0 and AppleALC 1.2.0 remained...<br><br>
Thanks to the actual changes by <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/933653/" class="" target="_blank">@vit9696</a> in the Lilu.kext v1.2.1 source distribution, Lilu.kext v1.2.1 now behaves again similar to v1.1.x and all KP issues totally vanished.<br><br>
To always access, download and compile the most actual but not yet officially released Lilu and Lilu plugin distributions, follow these links:<br><br>
a.) <a href="https://github.com/vit9696/Lilu" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fvit9696%2FLilu&amp;hash=1e68e9e14e62ea616bdce0cf1d6cb3e1" rel="nofollow">Lilu Source distribution</a><br>
b.) <a href="https://github.com/vit9696/AppleALC" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fvit9696%2FAppleALC&amp;hash=dbdc0b5cb966128ff0c2baaed4ac5b14" rel="nofollow">AppleALC Source Distribution</a><br>
c.) <a href="https://sourceforge.net/p/nvidiagraphicsfixup/svn/HEAD/tree/trunk/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fsourceforge.net%2Fp%2Fnvidiagraphicsfixup%2Fsvn%2FHEAD%2Ftree%2Ftrunk%2F&amp;hash=eef04b00f85adbb95826fdcece2a6cfc" rel="nofollow">NvidiaGraphicsFixup</a><br><br>
To successfully compile the AppleALC and NvidiaGraphicsFixup source code distributions with Xcode 9.2 under macOS High Sierra 10.13.2, download, unzip and copy the respective actual <a href="https://github.com/vit9696/Lilu/releases" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fvit9696%2FLilu%2Freleases&amp;hash=e81c6ef8460113bb770f1e669cb7c492" rel="nofollow">Lilu DEBUG</a> distribution to the AppleALC and NvidiaGraphicsFixup source code distribution directories. To compile the respective Lilu, AppleALC, and NvidiaGraphicsFixup source code distributions just execute the terminal command "<i>xcodebuild</i>" after changing to the respective source code distribution with the "<i>cd</i>" terminal command. The resulting compiled kexts can be always found in the respective /build/Release/ sub-directories of the respective source code distribution directories.<br><br>
Note the additional KernelToPatch entry to the config.plist contained in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> and  <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> in  the Kernel and Kext Patches Section of Clover Configurator<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Find: 8A 02 84 C0 74 44 &nbsp;Replace: 8A 02 84 C0 EB 44 &nbsp; &nbsp;Comment: Lilu 1.2.x Debug</div></div>for Lilu 1.2.x debug reasons.<br><br>
Further details to the topic can be accessed by following <a href="https://github.com/vit9696/Lilu/issues/30" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Fvit9696%2FLilu%2Fissues%2F30&amp;hash=24849d6e0bb12691ce0888e0b1074247" rel="nofollow">THIS LINK</a>.<br><br>
​</div>14.) To clearly get kernel panic images with a call trace in case of kernel panics, I implemented (checked) boot flags<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">"<i>debug=0x100</i>" and "<i>keepsyms=1</i>" in the config.plist of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> and <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118-zip.304121/?temp_hash=a4ebbf9ce07742393f51b4bb49a47c69" class="internalLink"></a><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> in the "Boot" Section of Clover Configurator under "Arguments".<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><b><br><span class="size5">D.) macOS 10.13 High Sierra System Setup</span></b>​</div></div></div></div></div></div><br>
Below, one finds a detailed description for the Clean Install of macOS High Sierra 10.13 or subsequent updates of the latter operating System.<br><br><span style="color: #ff0000">Please not once more that the  SMBIOS iMAC 17,1 system definition is absolutely mandatory to successfully install or update your macOS High Sierra systems, as the 10.13.2 MacOS Installer package has neither the iMacPro BoardID nor iMacPro Model Properties implemented in the respective PlatformSupport.plists. A modification of the macOS Installer package unfortunately is at odd with the actual board rules.<br><br>
We will therefore use the EFI-Folder contained in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> with the SMBIOS iMac17,1 System definition during the macOS Clean Install or MacOS Update and finally implement SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 during the Post-Installation Process at the beginning of Section E.) by means of the EFI-Folder contained in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a>. </span><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span class="size5"><b>D.1) macOS High Sierra 10.13 Clean Install</b><b>on Skylake-X/X299</b></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/clean-install-png.272790/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="data/attachments/227/227699-2a29a7f3d34919db347a80be96b61165.jpg" alt="clean-install.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br>
​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div>I suggest to follow the individual steps below to successfully setup the latest version of macOS High Sierra 10.13  on a virgin test drive of your choice (NVMe or SSD or HDD).<br><br>
1.) In order to perform a clean install of macOS High Sierra 10.13, prepare a USB Flash Drive (source, named USB) and a<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">NVMe or SDD or HDD destination drive fo your macOS installation by formatting both drives with HFS+ [(Mac OS Extended (Journaled)] and a GUID partition table by means of Apple's Disk Utility on any other Hackintosh or Mac of your choice. This will create an empty HFS+ Partition and a yet empty EFI-partition on each drive.​</div><br>
2.) Download the macOS High Sierra 10.13 full package installer from the <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/macos-high-sierra/id1246284741?mt=12" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fitunes.apple.com%2Fus%2Fapp%2Fmacos-high-sierra%2Fid1246284741%3Fmt%3D12&amp;hash=60429c980e65c0d8a8abd66d5b8a44ca" rel="nofollow">Mac App Store</a>.<br><br>
3.) Once the Installer is in the Application-directory of your system disk, connect your USB Flash Drive (named USB) and run<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the following terminal command:​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo /Applications/Install\ macOS\ High\ Sierra.app/Contents/Resources/createinstallmedia --volume /Volumes/USB --applicationpath /Applications/Install\ macOS\ High\ Sierra.app --nointeraction</div></div>Alternatively, one can create the macOS USB Flash Drive Installer also by means of the <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/install-disk-creator-app-zip.289144/?temp_hash=18451358e07b635b6fa62e661fbb19be" class="internalLink">Install Disk Creator.app</a><br>
​</div>4.) Now perform the following steps detailed below.<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Copy the EFI directory being part of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> (attached at the end of this<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">originating post/guide) to the empty EFI partitions of both your USB Flash Drive and your macOS Install destination drive (system disk). <span style="color: #000000">Remove the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi from the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/-directory of your USB Flash Drive Installer!<br><br>
Important additional note for all newbies (implemented on user request):<br></span><br>
The empty EFI-partitions can be mounted by means of e.g. <a href="http://mackie100projects.altervista.org/download-clover-configurator/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fmackie100projects.altervista.org%2Fdownload-clover-configurator%2F&amp;hash=e318f7fdbf1239e5200c6a38ce24f4b5" rel="nofollow">Clover Configurator</a>.<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/clover-configurator-png.282088/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/clover-configurator-png.282088/" alt="Clover -Configurator.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
Just select the "Mount" menu (1.), mount any partition displayed by means of "Mount Partition" (2.) and subsequently open it's EFI-Folder with "Open Partition" (3.). The latter function opens an Apple File Manager, which allows to copy, paste, delete anything on/to or from the respective EFI Partition. Ones your manipulation of the respective EFI-Folder is finished, select "unMount Partition" (4). By means of the latter command,  the EFI-Folder will be unmounted and disappear again. Don't forget that Clover Configurator is also a mighty tool for config.plist editing and configuration! We therefore will use it many times along this guide!<br>
​</div>b.) In case that EFI directory being part of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> once would not contain the most<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">actual clover distribution (which presently is not the case) download and install <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/cloverefiboot/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fsourceforge.net%2Fprojects%2Fcloverefiboot%2F&amp;hash=d0b1ed60cc55607c749fa6c5eb1291e9" rel="nofollow">the latest clover distribution</a> by verifying the proper Install-Location (again you have to do it twice for your USB Flash Drive and your System Disk) by customizing (don't press "Install" but "Customize" before) the following clover install-options:​</div><ul><li>Install for UEFI booting only</li></ul><ul><li>Install Clover in the ESP</li></ul><ul><li>Select the Bootloader Themes you want to install</li></ul><ul><li>Enable Install RC scripts on target volume</li></ul><ul><li>For the clover installation on your USB Flash Drive, check "CsmVideoDxe-64" under "Drivers64UEFI" (to comply with error prevention C.4.a.). For the clover installation on your system disk, check "CsmVideoDxe-64" and "EmuVariableUefi-64" under "Drivers64UEFI" (to comply with error convention C.4.b). Since Clover_v2.4k_r4233, also check "OsxAptioFixDrv-64" but uncheck all other EFI-driver options under "Drivers64UEFI" for the clover installation on both drives!</li></ul><ul><li>Select Install Clover Preference Pane</li></ul>c.) Open the config.plist on your system disk with the latest version of the Clover Configurator, proceed to the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">"SMBIOS" Section and complete the Serial Number, Board Serial Number and SMUUID entries as detailed below in order to successfully install and run macOS High Sierra 10.13 on your Skylake-X/X299 System, free of issues or limitations with respect to iMessage and Facetime Functionality. Note that you should maintain the iMac17,1 SMBIOS entries already implemented in the config.plist of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a>.<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div>i.) Press several times the "Generate New" Button next to serial number text field. Copy the serial number and<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">perform the serial number check on <a href="http://www.everymac.com/ultimate-mac-lookup/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.everymac.com%2Fultimate-mac-lookup%2F&amp;hash=5df4affb2c56af84043ed57c7e2f94c1" rel="nofollow">http://www.everymac.com/ultimate-mac-lookup/</a> by following <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/374452/" class="" target="_blank">@P1LGRIM</a> 's related instructions in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/an-idiots-guide-to-imessage.196827/" class="internalLink">"An iDiots's Guide To iMessage"</a>.<br>
​</div>ii.)
