Also perform the serial number check on <a href="https://checkcoverage.apple.com/gb/en/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fcheckcoverage.apple.com%2Fgb%2Fen%2F&amp;hash=1a29f40190921d26771cca21aa5f81a7" rel="nofollow">https://checkcoverage.apple.com/gb/en/</a> by following<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/374452/" class="" target="_blank">@P1LGRIM</a> 's related instructions in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/an-idiots-guide-to-imessage.196827/" class="internalLink">"An iDiots's Guide To iMessage"</a>.<br><br>
If all checks have been past successfully, proceed to point iii.) below.<br>
​</div>iii.) Note that the latest versions of Clover Configurator already correctly implements the Board Serial Number in<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">parallel. Thus one can skip the related description in@P1LGRIM 's  <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/an-idiots-guide-to-imessage.196827/" class="internalLink">"An iDiots's Guide To iMessage"</a>.<br>
​</div>iv.) In the final step, open a terminal, enter repeatedly the command "<i>uuidgen", </i>and copy the output value to<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the SMUUID field in the "SMBIOS" Section of the Clover Configurator.<br>
​</div></div>Save the config.plist on your system disk.<br><span style="color: #ff0000"><br>
The same procedure by the way also applies for the successful implementation of SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 contained in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> and described in Section E.)  "Post Installation Process".Note however, that the Serial Number Check on <a href="http://www.everymac.com" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.everymac.com&amp;hash=f69d8400e33b30d28825dabb95c12eaa" rel="nofollow">www.everymac.com</a> proposed in D.1.4.c.i.) apparently does not work yet for iMacPro, thus one needs to blindly believe in the iMacPro Serial Number and Board Serial Number generated by Clover Configurator.<br></span>​</div>d.) Transfer the correct Serial Number, Board Serial Number and SMUUID  also to the config.plist of your USB Flash Drive.<br><br>
e.) Verify that you have the correct apsf.efi file in the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/ directories of your USB Flash Drive and<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">System Disk by following error prevention C/9.).<br>
​</div>f.) Copy the appropriate VoodooTSCSync.kext, which you modified by following error prevention C/10.), to the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">/EFI/CLOVER/kexts/Other/ - directories of both USB Flash Drive and System Disk!<br>
​</div></div>Both drives are now ready for installation. Reboot your System.<br><br>
5.) While booting, press the F8 button to enter the BIOS boot menu. Select to boot from your USB Flash Drive.<br><br>
6.) Subsequently, click on the USB Flash Drive Icon in the clover boot menu to boot the respective macOS High Sierra Installer<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">on your USB Flash Drive.​</div><br>
7.) After successful boot, pass the individual steps of the macOS high Sierra 10.13 installation menu and finally select the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">destination drive of your macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installation, which should be logically the system disk you successfully configured above. In the next step, the Installer will create a macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Partition on the system disk and subsequently reboot your system.​</div><br>
8.) During system reboot, just press again the F8 button to enter the BIOS boot menu. Select again to boot from your USB<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Flash Drive. In contrary to 6.), click this time on the "Install MacOS on Drive XXX" Icon on the clover boot screen to boot the newly created macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Partition on your system disk.​</div><br>
9.) After successful boot, you will enter now the macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Screen with a progress bar starting at<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">18 minutes. This is normally also the moment when either error 3.) or 4a.) occurs if you did not properly follow my instructions for error prevention above. In any case, if everything goes fine and there is no error message, the installer will again reboot your System just after a few couple of minutes. Don't be scared, this just seems to be part of the correct overall installation procedure!<br>
​</div>10.) During system reboot press again the F8 button to enter the BIOS boot menu. Select again to boot from your USB<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Flash Drive. Click again on the "Install MacOS on Drive XXX" Icon on the clover boot screen to boot once more the macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Partition on your system disk!<br>
​</div>11.) After successful boot, you will enter once more the macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Screen with the progress bar<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">starting now at about 41 minutes of remaining installation time. This time is actually really roughly also the time the subsequent installation will require. When approaching a remaining time of 17 minutes for installation, the installer will once more reboot your System!​</div><br>
12.) <span style="color: #000000">Now the important final step of the macOS install procedure as commented already several times before!</span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">During the last </span></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">system </span><span style="color: #000000">reboot towards the end of the MacOS installation process, press again the F8 button to enter the BIOS boot menu. However, in the BIOS boot menu select this time to boot from your system disk, with the EFI-folder that also contains the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi file (this is fundamental for a the correct registration of your system in iCloud, as the final requisite of the entire macOS installation process) and subsequently select and boot the new macOS High Sierra 10.13 Partition on your 10.13 system disk in the Clover Boot menu. By booting the final step of the macOS High Sierra Clean Install process without the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi in the EFI-Folder (remember that we omitted on purpose this efi-file in the EFI-Folder of the USB Flash Drive Installer to fulfill error prevention 4.a), your "ROM" and "Board Serial Number" SMBIOS confidential would be erroneously transmitted to iCloud because of the SMBIOS iMac17,1 definition and the fact that you use a X299 board. In case of transmitting erroneous SMBIOS information, you will be able to register your System in iCloud, like nothing would have happened or failed.. However when subsequently trying to use "iMessage" or "Facetime" on your system drive, you will not be able to perform the once more requested registration with your correct Apple-ID and Password in order to successfully run the two latter Apple Services. As already indicated under error prevention 4b.), the latter issue only can be solved by signing out from iCloud, by previously unchecking in Apple's Photos Application under "Preferences" the options "iCloud Photo Library", "My Photo Stream" and "iCloud Photo Sharing", and by subsequently repeating all necessary steps detailed in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/374452/" class="" target="_blank">@P1LGRIM</a> 's </span><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/an-idiots-guide-to-imessage.196827/" class="internalLink"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">"An iDiots's Guide To iMessage"</span></a><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"> by considering also my additional modifications and comments detailed under D.1/4.c) and D1/4.d) above! </span>​</div><br>
13.) After successfully completing the iCloud registration, you now successfully finished the macOS High Sierra Clean<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Installation Process on your X299 / Skylake-X System, unless you want to still want to migrate data and programs from a system different from your current Skylake-X/X299 build.<br>
​</div>14.) Continue with the Post Installation Process detailed in Section E.) below.<br><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span class="size5"><b>D.2)</b><b>macOS High Sierra 10.13 Upgrade</b><b>on Skylake-X/X299</b></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/upgrade-1-png.276782/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="data/attachments/231/231691-18c21b2de445d04e4e7f9e954fd83fa7.jpg" alt="upgrade-1.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a>
			
​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div>If you already previously successfully performed a macOS High Sierra 10.13 Clean Install or Upgrade to a more advanced macOS High Sierra Distribution on your Skylake-X/X299 System and you now want to provide your System with latest version of macOS High Sierra 10.13, follow all suggestions indicated below.<br><br>
1.) Backup the EFI-Folders of both previous USB Flash Drive Installer and 10.13 System Disk. Also backup your 10.13 System<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Disk itself, e.g. by cloning your current 10.13 System Disk by means of Carbon Copy Cloner (CCC).​</div><br>
2.) In order to perform the update of macOS High Sierra 10.13, format your former USB Flash Drive (source, named USB) with<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">HFS+ [(Mac OS Extended (Journaled)] and a GUID partition table by means of Apple's Disk Utility.​</div><br>
3.) Download the macOS High Sierra 10.13 full package installer from the <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/macos-high-sierra/id1246284741?mt=12" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fitunes.apple.com%2Fus%2Fapp%2Fmacos-high-sierra%2Fid1246284741%3Fmt%3D12&amp;hash=60429c980e65c0d8a8abd66d5b8a44ca" rel="nofollow">Mac App Store</a>.  Once the Installer is in the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">"Application" directory of your system disk, connect your USB Flash Drive (named USB) and run the following terminal command:​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo /Applications/Install\ macOS\ High\ Sierra.app/Contents/Resources/createinstallmedia --volume /Volumes/USB --applicationpath /Applications/Install\ macOS\ High\ Sierra.app --nointeraction</div></div>Alternatively, on can create the macOS USB Flash Drive Installer also again by means of the <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/install-disk-creator-app-zip.289144/?temp_hash=18451358e07b635b6fa62e661fbb19be" class="internalLink">Install Disk Creator.app</a><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div></div>4.) Now perform the following steps detailed below.<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">a.) Replace the former EFI-directories of both USB Flash Drive Installer and 10.13 System Disk with the EFI-directory being<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">part of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> (attached towards the end of of this originating post/guide). Remove the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi from the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/-directory of your USB Flash Drive Installer to comply with error prevention C/4.a)!<br>
​</div>b.) In case that this EFI-Folder once would not contain the most actual clover distribution (which presently is not the case),<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">download and install <a href="https://sourceforge.net/projects/cloverefiboot/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fsourceforge.net%2Fprojects%2Fcloverefiboot%2F&amp;hash=d0b1ed60cc55607c749fa6c5eb1291e9" rel="nofollow">the latest clover distribution</a> on both, your USB Flash Drive and 10.13 System Disk by verifying the proper clover install location and by customizing (don't press "Install" but "Customize" before) the following clover install options:​</div><ul><li>Install for UEFI booting only</li></ul><ul><li>Install Clover in the ESP</li></ul><ul><li>Select the Bootloader Themes you want to install</li></ul><ul><li>Enable Install RC scripts on target volume</li></ul><ul><li>For the clover installation on your USB Flash Drive, check "CsmVideoDxe-64" under "Drivers64UEFI" (to comply with error prevention C.4.a.). For the clover installation on your system disk, check "CsmVideoDxe-64" and "EmuVariableUefi-64" under "Drivers64UEFI" (to comply with error convention C.4.b). Since Clover_v2.4k_r4233, also check "OsxAptioFixDrv-64" but uncheck all other EFI-driver options under "Drivers64UEFI" for the clover installation on both drives!</li></ul><ul><li>Select Install Clover Preference Pane</li></ul>c.) Open the config.plist on your USB Flash Drive and 10.13 System Disk, proceed to the "SMBIOS" Section and complete<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the yet empty Serial Number, Board Serial Number and SMUUID entries with your particular personal values derived during the initial clean install of MacOS High Sierra 10.13 detailed in D.1/4.c).<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div></div>Save the config.plists on your USB Flash Drive and 10.13 System Disk.​</div></div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">d.) Verify that you have the correct apsf.efi file in the /EFI/CLOVER/drivers64UEFI/ directories of your USB Flash Drive and<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">System Disk by following error prevention C/9.).<br>
​</div>e.) Copy the appropriate VoodooTSCSync.kext, which you modified by following error prevention C/10.), to the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">/EFI/CLOVER/kexts/Other/ - directories of both USB Flash Drive and System Disk!​</div></div><br>
Both drives are now ready for MacOS upgrade. Reboot your System.<br><br>
5.) While booting, press the F8 button to enter the BIOS boot menu. Select to boot from your USB Flash Drive.<br><br>
6.) Subsequently, click on the USB Flash Drive Icon in the clover boot menu to boot the respective macOS High Sierra Installer<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">on your USB Flash Drive.​</div><br>
7.) After successful boot, pass the individual steps of the macOS high Sierra 10.13 installation menu and finally select the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">destination drive of your macOS High Sierra 10.13 Update, which should be logically your 10.13 System Disk. In the next step, the Installer will create a macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Partition on your 10.13 System Disk and subsequently reboot your system.​</div><br>
8.) During system reboot, just press again the F8 button to enter the BIOS boot menu. Select again to boot from your USB<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Flash Drive. In contrary to 6.), click this time on the "Install MacOS on Drive XXX" Icon on the clover boot screen to boot the newly created macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Partition on your 10.13 System Disk.​</div><br>
9.) After successful boot, you will enter now the macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Screen with a progress bar starting at<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">18 minutes. This is normally also the moment when either error C/3.) or C/4.a) occurs if you did not properly follow my instructions for error prevention in C/3.) and C/4.a). In any case, if everything goes fine and there is no error message, the installer will again reboot your System just after a few couple of minutes. Don't be scared, this just seems to be part of the correct overall installation procedure!<br>
​</div>10.) During system reboot press again the F8 button to enter the BIOS boot menu. Select again to boot from your USB<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Flash Drive. Click again on the "Install MacOS on Drive XXX" Icon on the clover boot screen to boot once more the macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Partition on your 10.13 System Disk.<br>
​</div>11.) After successful boot, you will enter once more the macOS High Sierra 10.13 Installer Screen with the progress bar<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">starting now at about 34 minutes of remaining installation time. This time is actually really roughly also the time the subsequent installation will require. When approaching a remaining time of 17 minutes for installation, the installer will once more reboot your System!​</div><br>
12.) <span style="color: #000000">Now the important final step of the macOS update procedure as commented already several times before!</span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">During the last </span></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">system </span><span style="color: #000000">reboot towards the end of the MacOS update process, press again the F8 button to enter the </span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">BIOS boot menu. However, in the BIOS boot menu select this time to boot from your system disk, with the EFI-folder that also contains the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi file (this is fundamental for a the correct registration of your system in iCloud, as the final requisite of the entire macOS installation process) and subsequently select and boot the macOS High Sierra 10.13 Partition on your 10.13 system disk in the Clover Boot menu. By booting the final step of the macOS High Sierra Upgrade process without the EmuVariableUefi-64.efi in the EFI-Folder (remember that we omitted on purpose this efi-file in the EFI-Folder of the USB Flash Drive Installer to fulfill error prevention 4.a), your "ROM" and "Board Serial Number" SMBIOS confidential would be erroneously transmitted to iCloud because of the SMBIOS iMac17,1 system definition and the fact that you use a X299 board. In case of transmitting erroneous SMBIOS information, you will be able to register your System in iCloud, like nothing would have happened or failed.. However when subsequently trying to use "iMessage" or "Facetime" on your system drive, you will not be able to perform the once more requested registration with your correct Apple-ID and Password in order to successfully run the two latter Apple Services. As already indicated under error prevention 4b.), the latter issue only can be solved by signing out from iCloud, by previously unchecking in Apple's Photos Application under "Preferences" the options "iCloud Photo Library", "My Photo Stream" and "iCloud Photo Sharing", and by subsequently repeating all necessary steps detailed in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/374452/" class="" target="_blank">@P1LGRIM</a> 's </span><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/an-idiots-guide-to-imessage.196827/" class="internalLink"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">"An iDiots's Guide To iMessage"</span></a><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"> by considering also my additional modifications and comments detailed under D.1/4.c) above!</span>​</div><br>
13.) After successfully completing the iCloud registration, you now successfully finished the macOS High Sierra Update Process<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">on your X299 / Skylake-X System.<br>
​</div>14.) All Nvidia Graphics Cards Users will have to install the update the Web Driver as detailed in Section E.) below.<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>
​</div><span class="size5"><b>D.3)</b><b>macOS High Sierra 10.13 Upgrade from macOS Sierra 10.12.6 on Skylake-X/X299 </b></span>​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/10-12-png.284079/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/10-12-png.284079/" alt="10.12.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a>
		
​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><br>
If you previously installed macOS Sierra 10.12.6 on your Skylake-X/X299 System by means of my <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/skylake-x-x299-live-the-future-now-on-macos-sierra-10-12-successful-build-extended-guide.229354/#post-1561330" class="internalLink">Skylake-X/X299 macOS Sierra 10.12 Desktop Guide</a>, the subsequent update to macOS High Sierra 10.13 is quite straight and easy, once the mandatory 10.13 EFI-Folder has been derived by following D.1.4.a) to D.1.4.f)!<br><br>
1.)  Prepare a USB Flash Drive (source, named USB) and a NVMe or SDD or HDD clone drive by formatting both drives with<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">HFS+ [(Mac OS Extended (Journaled)] and a GUID partition table by means of Apple's Disk Utility on your 10.12.6 Skylake-X/X299 Hackintosh or Mac of your choice. This will create an empty HFS+ Partition and a yet empty EFI-partition on each drive.​</div><br>
2.) Clone your current macOS 10.12.6 System Disk by means of Carbon Copy Cloner (CCC) to the NVMe or SDD or HDD clone<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">drive which we will term hereafter 10.13 System Disk.​</div><br>
3.) Download the macOS High Sierra 10.13 full package installer from the <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/macos-high-sierra/id1246284741?mt=12" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fitunes.apple.com%2Fus%2Fapp%2Fmacos-high-sierra%2Fid1246284741%3Fmt%3D12&amp;hash=60429c980e65c0d8a8abd66d5b8a44ca" rel="nofollow">Mac App Store</a>.<br><br>
4.) Once the Installer is in the Application-directory of your system disk, connect your USB Flash Drive (named USB) and run<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the following terminal command:​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo /Applications/Install\ macOS\ High\ Sierra.app/Contents/Resources/createinstallmedia --volume /Volumes/USB --applicationpath /Applications/Install\ macOS\ High\ Sierra.app --nointeraction</div></div></div><br>
5.) Now create the 10.13 EFI-Folder on your USB macOS Flash Drive Installer and 10.13 System Disk (former 10.12.6 System<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Disk Clone Drive) by following steps D.1.4.a) to D.1.4.f)! During this procedure you can also certainly merge already existing config.plist details with the config.plist contained in the EFI-Folder of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a> and skip all related steps in this part of the guide [e.g. D.1.4.c.), i.e.  Board Serial Number, Serial Number and SmUUID, if already available from the previous 10.12.6 installation].<br><br>
Both drives are now ready for the MacOS upgrade. Reboot your System.<br>
​</div>6.) Now perform the MacOS High Sierra Upgrade by following point 5.) to 13.) of section D.2) [macOS High Sierra 10.13 Clean<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Install]​</div><br>
7.) Subsequently, perform all necessary steps of section E.) "Post Installation Process" detailed below!<br><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span class="size5"><b>E.) Post Installation Process</b></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/post-installation-png.272809/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="data/attachments/227/227718-44a74965f9ffa537647ee212df997f1f.jpg" alt="post-installation.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a>
			
​</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><br><span style="color: #ff0000">To successfully boot your Skylake-X/X299 System with the SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 system definition, copy the attached <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/platformsupport-plist-zip.303116/?temp_hash=c9606d566f7ffab6bceb34a4a462240a" class="internalLink">PlatformSupport.plist</a> to /System/Library/CoreServices/.<br><br>
You can also copy the /System/Library/CoreServices/PlatformSupport.plist to your Desktop, directly add "BoardID Mac-7BA5B2D9E42DDD94" under SupportedBoardIds and "iMacPro1,1" under SupportedModelProperties by means of Xcode as suggested by user Griven from the German Hackintosh-Forum and copy back the modified PlatformSupport.plist to System/Library/CoreServices/.</span><br><br><span style="color: #ff0000">For the final SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 implementation, exchange the SMBIOS iMac17,1 EFI-Folder on your 10.13 System Disk by the one contained in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> and complete the latter SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 EFI-Folder in concordance with your former System Disk EFI-Folder. Alternatively, you can simply transfer all SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 details contained in the EFI-Folder of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> to your actual System Disk EFI-Folder, which has been implemented ind Section D.) above by means of  <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118-zip.304122/?temp_hash=a4ebbf9ce07742393f51b4bb49a47c69" class="internalLink"></a><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imac17-1-070118a-zip.304239/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMac17,1-070118a.zip</a>p, which else is identical  with <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a>. <br><br>
Don't forget to add the SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 Serial Number, Board Serial Number and SMUUID as described in D.1.4.c) for SMBIOS iMac17,1. Note however, that the Serial Number Check on <a href="http://www.everymac.com" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.everymac.com&amp;hash=f69d8400e33b30d28825dabb95c12eaa" rel="nofollow">www.everymac.com</a> proposed in D.1.4.c.i.) apparently does not work yet for iMacPro, thus one needs to blindly believe in the iMacPro Serial Number and Board Serial Number generated by Clover Configurator.   <br><br>
Subsequently, reboot your system which now will officially figure as iMacPro. </span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>
​</div><span class="size4"><b>E1.)</b><b><b><b>X</b>nu <b>C</b>PU <b>P</b>ower <b>M</b>anagement</b> (XCPM) Configuration</b></span><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/power-management-png.272852/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="data/attachments/227/227761-90334a736495a105fe37f9eb6eb29e48.jpg" alt="power-management.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
The EFI folder of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> attached towards the end of this originating post/guide, already contains a fully functional XCPM configuration for all Skylake-X processors! And the excellent news are that XCPM is performing nearly native on Skylake-X/X299 systems. One just has to perform one single step to successfully run XCPM on the freshly installed Skylake-X/X299 system. Remember the necessity of the correct BIOS settings for each board detailed at the beginning of this guide.<br><br>
When inspecting the config.plist in the EFI-folder of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118-zip.304121/?temp_hash=a4ebbf9ce07742393f51b4bb49a47c69" class="internalLink"></a><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a> (attached at the end of this originating post/guide) with the Clover Configurator, one immediately realises that there are just a view necessary patches to improve the overall XCPM performance or to properly display the Skylake-X properties in Apple's System Overview.<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div>a.) The "FakeCPUID entry" in the Kernel and Kext Patches Section of the clover configurator (still required for e.g. the i9-<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">7980XE, already not required for e.g. the i7-7820X or i9-7900X).<br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/fakecpuid-png.272829/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/fakecpuid-png.272829/" alt="FakeCPUID.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br>
​</div>b.) Note that the only XCPM KernelToPatch entry not disabled in the "Kernel and Kext Patches Section of the Clover<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Conifgurator" is xcpm_core_scope_msrs, which is still required because of the MSR Lock in the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe  BIOS ...  All other disabled KernelToPatch entries are natively supported by OSX!​</div></div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div style="padding-left: 30px"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/xcpm-entry-png.272833/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/xcpm-entry-png.272833/" alt="xcpm-entry.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a>
		
​</div></div><br><span style="text-decoration: underline">How to finalize the Skylake-X/X299 XCPM configuration (note that steps 2 to 4 are not required anymore for e.g. the i7-7820X or i9-7900X):</span><br><br>
1.) Verify with the terminal command "<i>sysctl machdep.xcpm.mode</i>" if the XCPM mode is active. If so,<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">"<i>sysctl machdep.xcpm.mode</i>" should return "1".​</div><br>
2.) Download Pike Alpha's <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssdtprgen-sh-imacpro-zip.303117/?temp_hash=c9606d566f7ffab6bceb34a4a462240a" class="internalLink">ssdtPRGen.sh-iMacPro</a> distribution attached at the bottom of this originating post/guide, which I recently modified for  iMacPro1,1 SMBIOS and iMacPro1,1 BoardID compatibly.<br><br>
3.) Drop ssdtPRGen.sh into a terminal and add the flag "-turbo 4400", in case the turbo stock speed of<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">your Skylake-X processor is 4400 MHz, like in case of the i9-7980XE. Adopt the value in compatibility with the turbo stock speed of your particular Skylake-X CPU.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">./ssdtPRGen.sh &nbsp;-turbo 4400</div></div>Result:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
ssdtPRGen.sh v0.9 &nbsp;Copyright (c) 2011-2012 by † RevoGirl<br>
[INDENT][INDENT] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;v6.6 &nbsp;Copyright (c) 2013 by † Jeroen<br>
[INDENT][INDENT]v21.5 Copyright (c) 2013-2018 by Pike R. Alpha[/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT]<br>
-----------------------------------------------------------<br><br>
Bugs &gt; https://github.com/Piker-Alpha/ssdtPRGen.sh/issues &lt;<br><br>
System information: Mac OS X 10.13.2 (17C88)<br>
Brandstring: "Intel(R) Core(TM) i9-7980XE CPU @ 2.60GHz"<br><br>
Override value: (-turbo) maximum (turbo) frequency, now using: 4400 MHz!<br><br>
Version: models.cfg v171 / Skylake.cfg v195<br><br>
Generating ssdt.dsl for a 'iMacPro1,1' with board-id [Mac-7BA5B2D9E42DDD94]<br>
Skylake Core i9-7980XE processor [0x50654] setup [0x0705]<br>
With a maximum TDP of 165 Watt, as specified by Intel<br>
Number logical CPU's: 36 (Core Frequency: 2600 MHz)<br>
Number of Turbo States: 18 (2700-4400 MHz)<br>
Number of P-States: 37 (800-4400 MHz)<br>
Injected C-States for CP00 (C1,C3,C6,C7,C8,C9,C10)<br>
Injected C-States for CP01 (C1,C2,C3,C6,C7)<br>

[INDENT][INDENT] &nbsp; &nbsp;- Clover users should read https://clover-wiki.zetam.org/Configuration/CPU#cpu_type[/INDENT][/INDENT]<br>
Compiling: ssdt_pr.dsl<br>
Intel ACPI Component Architecture<br>
ASL Optimizing Compiler version 20140926-64 [Nov &nbsp;6 2014]<br>
Copyright (c) 2000 - 2014 Intel Corporation<br><br>
ASL Input: &nbsp; &nbsp; /Users/kgp/Library/ssdtPRGen/ssdt.dsl - 730 lines, 20774 bytes, 241 keywords<br>

Compilation complete. 0 Errors, 0 Warnings, 0 Remarks, 0 Optimizations<br>
Do you want to open ssdt.dsl (y/n)? n<br>
&nbsp;</div></div><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div></div>4.) Copy the SSDT.aml from ~/Library/ssdtPRGen/ to the /EFI/CLOVER/ACPI/patched/ directory of your system disk and<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">reboot​</div><br>
5.) a.) Verify that in the ioRegistryExplorer you have now under CP00@0 the following entry:<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Property: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Type: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Value:<br>
plugin-type &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Number &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;0x1</div></div></div><br>
b.) Verify with the terminal command<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">kextstat|grep -y x86plat</div></div>that the "<i>X86PlatformPlugin.kext" </i>is now loaded. If the command returns something like<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">112 &nbsp; &nbsp;1 0xffffff7f822bc000 0x17000 &nbsp; &nbsp;0x17000 &nbsp; &nbsp;com.apple.driver.X86PlatformPlugin (1.0.0) FD88AF70-3E2C-3935-99E4-C48669EC274B &lt;111 19 18 13 11 7 6 5 4 3 1&gt;<br>
146 &nbsp; &nbsp;1 0xffffff7f822d3000 0x7000 &nbsp; &nbsp; 0x7000 &nbsp; &nbsp; com.apple.driver.X86PlatformShim (1.0.0) DCEA94A4-3547-3129-A888-E9D5C77B275E &lt;112 111 13 7 4 3&gt;</div></div>your are fine.​</div><br>
c.) Verify with the terminal command<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">kextstat|grep -y appleintelcpu</div></div>that the Apple Intel CPU power management is not loaded. If the result is empty you are fine.​</div><br>
d.) Verify with the following terminal command:<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sysctl -n machdep.xcpm.vectors_loaded_count</div></div>that the Frequency-Vectors for the iMacPro1,1 are loaded. If the result is "1" you are fine. Note that there is no necessity for the additional injection of a Frequency-Vector in case of SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 as the related plist file already carries the Frequency-Vector definition.​</div><br>
6.) To deeply investigate your final XCPM functionality,  download Piker Alpha’s <a href="https://github.com/Piker-Alpha/AppleIntelInfo" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2FPiker-Alpha%2FAppleIntelInfo&amp;hash=09a5252e9c470c0c130c84e3b3b1d9f5" rel="nofollow">AppleIntelInfo.kext</a> from Github. To compile<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the source code, you need to primarily install Xcode (Appstore) and Xcode Command Line Tools! <a href="http://railsapps.github.io/xcode-command-line-tools.html" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Frailsapps.github.io%2Fxcode-command-line-tools.html&amp;hash=b0dedc831d9f215ac51d3d125a429262" rel="nofollow">This guideline</a> might be helpful for the successfully installation of the latter. <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: underline">Important Note:</span></span><span style="color: #000000">AppleIntelInfo.kext is not yet compatible with the i9-7980XE! Executing the terminal command  "sudo kextload AppleIntelInfo.kext" will result in an immediate reboot of your i9-7980XE/X299 System!</span><br><br>
Now enter the following terminal commands:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">cd ~/Downloads/AppleIntelInfo-master<br>
xcodebuild<br>
cd build/Release<br>
chmod -R 755 AppleIntelInfo.kext<br>
sudo chown -R root:wheel AppleIntelInfo.kext</div></div>Load the AppleIntelInfo.kext with "kextload" and "cat" the info-results with the following terminal commands:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo kextload AppleIntelInfo.kext</div></div><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo cat /tmp/AppleIntelInfo.dat</div></div>The cat command should reveal something like the following result (note that due to the incompatibility of AppleIntelInfo.kext with the i9-7980XE, the implemented results still refer to the i7-7800X, which I used within my starter configuration):<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">AppleIntelInfo.kext v2.6 Copyright © 2012-2017 Pike R.
