Your Thunderbolt EX3 PCIe Adapter and connected devices should be now fully implemented and</span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">functional.</span><br>
​</div><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">12.) Finally note that there is no Hot Plug Support with the current configuration. Thus related Thunderbolt Devices must</span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">be connected before System Boot and cannot be unplugged or replugged during system operation!</span><br><br>
​</div><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span class="size4">Thunderbolt Benchmark</span></span></b><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">For the sake fo completeness and for testing the overall Thunderbolt Functionality and Performance, I benchmarked the the data rates of an external Thunderbolt Drive connected via Apple's Thunderbolt-3 to Thunderbolt-2 Adapter. As External Thunderbolt Drive, I once more used the Lacie Rugged Thunderbolt / USB Type-A and Type-C HDD.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/thunderbolt-ex3-pcie-_-lacie-png.276391/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/thunderbolt-ex3-pcie-_-lacie-png.276391/" alt="Thunderbolt EX3 PCIe _ Lacie.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span><br><span style="color: #000000"><br></span><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span class="size4"></span></span><span class="size4"><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">E.6) NVMe configuration</span></b></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>​</div><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/evo-png.276327/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/evo-png.276327/" alt="evo.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">In contrary to macOS Sierra 10.12, in macOS High Sierra 10.13 there is native support of non-4Kn NVMe SSDs, like my Samsung EVO 960 M.2 NVME. All patches applied under macOS Sierra 10.12 are therefore obsolete. The native support of non-4Kn NVMe SSDs enables the unique opportunity to directly perform a clean-install of macOS High Sierra 10.13 on M.2 NVMEs like the Samsung EVO 960.</span><br><br><span style="color: #000000">Even the tiny bug of an external drive implementation of NVMEs apparently has been fixed by Apple already within the macOS High Sierra 10.13 Supplemental Update (SU). Thus, the patches to circumvent the NVMe External Drive Implementation detailed below are now obsolete.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">1.) The NVMe External issue, was previously circumvented by adding an External NVME Icon KextToPatch</span></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: #000000"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">entry to the config.plist within Clover Configurator.</span></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Name* &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Find* [HEX] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace* [HEX] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Comment &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;MatchOS[/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S][/S]<br>
[S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S][S]IONVMeFamily &nbsp; &nbsp; 4885c074 07808b20 &nbsp; &nbsp; 4885c090 90808b20 &nbsp; &nbsp; External NVME Icon Patch &nbsp; &nbsp; 10.13.x</div></div></span></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/external-icon-patch-png.274137/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/external-icon-patch-png.274137/" alt="External-Icon-Patch.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span></span><br><br><span style="color: #000000"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">Note however, that already previously this patch did not seem to work anymore. Thus, there was another workaround,  detailed in 2.)</span></span><br>
​</div><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">2.) The second NVMe External Fix detailed below worked in 100%, although was a bit more tricky...</span></span><br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">a.) Disable the not working External NVME Icon KextToPatch entry.</span></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">b.) Open the IORegistryExplorer, in the upright search field type nvme and take note of values in the left column, i.e.</span></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">indicated as v.1, v.2 and v.3 and marked by red rectangles in the figure below. As you can see by following these entries, your nvme device shows up in PC00@0 &gt; RP09@1D &gt; PXSX@0</span><br><span style="text-decoration: line-through"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/nvme-external-patch-png.274141/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/nvme-external-patch-png.274141/" alt="NVMe-External-Patch.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span></span><br><span style="text-decoration: line-through"><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">Download and unzip the </span><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssdt-nvme-extern-icon-patch-aml-zip.274152/?temp_hash=adc2053f519f87ccf898615d1951a851" class="internalLink">SSDT-NVMe-extern-icon-patch.aml.zip</a><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">, and open the SSDT-NVMe-extern-icon-patch.aml<br>
with </span><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/maciasl-dsdt-app-zip.274151/?temp_hash=adc2053f519f87ccf898615d1951a851" class="internalLink">MaciASL-DSDT.app</a><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">, both attached towards the end of this guide. For deviating system configurations, replace the values highlighted in blue color in the figure below with those of your IOreg, marked by red rectangles and indicated by v.1, v.2 and v.3 in the figure of my IOReg above.</span></span><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssdt_nvme-external-png.274145/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssdt_nvme-external-png.274145/" alt="SSDT_NVME-EXTERNAL.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span></span><br>
​</div><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">c.) Save and copy the modified SSDT-NVMe-extern-icon-patch.aml to the /EFI/CLOVER/ACPI/patched/ folder of your</span></span><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">system drive.</span></span><br>
​</div></div><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span style="text-decoration: line-through">3.) Reboot</span></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">Your NVMe drive should show up correctly as internal.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/nvme-correct-1-png.274147/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/nvme-correct-1-png.274147/" alt="NVMe-correct-1.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/nvme-correct-2-png.274150/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/nvme-correct-2-png.274150/" alt="NVMe-correct-2.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span><br><span style="color: #000000"><br></span><br><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span class="size4">E.7.) SSD TRIM Support:</span></span></b><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">Macs only enable TRIM for Apple-provided solid-state drives they come with. If you upgrade a Mac with an aftermarket SSD, the Mac won’t use TRIM with it. The same applies for SSD's used by a Hackintosh. When an operating system uses TRIM with a solid-state drive, it sends a signal to the SSD every time you delete a file. The SSD knows that the file is deleted and it can erase the file’s data from its flash storage. With flash memory, it’s faster to write to empty memory — to write to full memory, the memory must first be erased and then written to. This causes your SSD to slow down over time unless TRIM is enabled. TRIM ensures the physical NAND memory locations containing deleted files are erased before you need to write to them. The SSD can then manage its available storage more intelligently.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">Note that the config.plist in the EFI-folder of </span><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"> attached towards the end of this guide, contains an SSD "TRIM Enabler" KextsToPatch entry, which can be found in the " Kernel and Kext Patches" Section of the Clover Configurator.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssd-trim-png.274131/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssd-trim-png.274131/" alt="SSD-Trim.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Name* &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[HEX] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Replace*[HEX] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Comment &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; MatchOS<br>
IOAHCIBlockStorage &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;4150504c 45205353 4400 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;00000000 00000000 0000 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Trim Enabler &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;10.12.x,10.13.x</div></div></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">With this KextToPatch entry, SSD TRIM should be  fully enabled on your 10.13 System, see Apple's System Report below.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssd-trim-2-png.274132/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssd-trim-2-png.274132/" alt="SSD-TRIM-2.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span class="size4"></span></span><span class="size4"><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">NVMe and SSD  Benchmark</span></b></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">For the sake of completeness please find below the Benchmark of connected NVMe and SDD Drives.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/diskspeed-png.276392/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/diskspeed-png.276392/" alt="diskspeed.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span><br><span style="color: #000000"><br></span><br><b><span style="font-family: 'Verdana'"><span class="size4">E.8) ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe on-board Ethernet-Functionality</span></span></b><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ehternet-png-276091-png.276393/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ehternet-png-276091-png.276393/" alt="ehternet-png.276091.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span><br><br><span style="font-family: 'Verdana'">Thanks to the <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/smalltree-intel-211-at-pcie-gbe-kext-zip.289090/?temp_hash=e5025470ac2a1f751e68a57b915e50c5" class="internalLink">SmallTree-Intel-211-AT-PCIe-GBE.kex</a>t, also the Intel I211_AT Gigabit on-board LAN controller of the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe will be correctly implemented and fully functional, in addition to the anyway natively implemented Intel I219-V Gigabyte on-board LAN controller of the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe. Thus, both ethernet ports on the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe should now be fully operational..</span><br><br><span style="font-family: 'Verdana'">Just download , unzip  and copy the <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/smalltree-intel-211-at-pcie-gbe-kext-zip.289090/?temp_hash=e5025470ac2a1f751e68a57b915e50c5" class="internalLink">SmallTree-Intel-211-AT-PCIe-GBE.kex</a> attached below to the /EFI/Clover/kexts/Other/, reboot and you should be done.</span><br><br><br><b><span class="size4">E.9) <b>ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe PCI Device Implementation - Sleep/Wake functionality</b></span></b><br><br>
In order to properly implement all PCI devices available on your system and build, one needs an adequate ACPI DSDT Replacement Patch Table and a sophisticated SSDT-X299.aml<i>. </i>Both requirements have been originally successfully implemented for the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe by our gorgeous <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/190386/" class="" target="_blank">@apfelnico</a> with partial contributions of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/1401507/" class="" target="_blank">@TheOfficialGypsy</a> . Many thanks for the extensive efforts and extremely fruitful and brilliant work!<br><span style="color: #ff0000">I now adopted the ACPI DSDT Replacement Patches and the SSDT-X299.aml in concordance with SMBIOS iMacPro1,1</span>. <span style="color: #ff0000">The updated ACPI DSDT Replacement Patches are already part of the config.plist contained in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a>. The new <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssdt-x299-imacpro-aml-zip.304028/?temp_hash=d856860230e0446e324db4e2364083ec" class="internalLink">SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml</a> is attached  at the bottom of this originating post/guide.</span><br><br>
Note that both ACPI DSDT Replacement Patches and SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml can be build and PCIe slot population dependend and have to be verified and likely adopted or modified for all mainboards different from the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe and builds or PCIe slot populations different from the one that constitutes the baseline of this guide.<br><br>
For the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe I will use in the following the PCIe Slot nomenclature depicted below:<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/asusprimex299deluxe-pci-slot-nomenclature-png.303192/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="data/attachments/258/258101-35422b2791fd35bcfd93a81a00c3adeb.jpg" alt="ASUSPrimeX299Deluxe-PCI-Slot-Nomenclature.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
The verification and likely adaptation/modification can be performed by the help of IORegistryExplorer v1.2. Note once more that the ACPI DSDT Replacement Patches and SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml implementation detailed below requires SMBIOS iMacPro1,1.<br><br><br><b><span class="size4">E.9.1)  ACPI DSDT Replacement Implementation</span></b><br><br>
Note that all required ACPI DSDT Patches are already implemented in the config.plist in the /EFI/CLOVER/ directory of the EFI-Folder contained in <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/efi-x299-10-13-2-release-imacpro1-1-070118a-zip.304238/?temp_hash=f325caa6971ec4f12840ad535b91967e" class="internalLink">EFI-X299-10.13.2-Release-iMacPro1,1-070118a.zip</a>. However, by default they are disabled, thus we will now open the config.plist in the /EFI/CLOVER/ directory of your 10.13 System Disk EFI-Folder with Clover Configurator and stepwise adopt (if necessary) and enable the different required DSDT replacement patches in Clover Configurator Section "ACPI" under "DSDT patches", by also discussing their respective function and impact.<br><br>
a.) The CAVS -&gt; HDEF DSDT replacement patch is audio related and has the aim to achieve the SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 specific HDEF<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">onboard audio controller implementation.<br><br>
If not already enabled in Section E.3), please enable this DSDT replacement patch now independent from your mainboard.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace [Hex]<br>
CAVS -&gt; HDEF &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;43415653 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 48444546<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div><br>
b.) The PC00 -&gt; PCI0 ACPI DSDT replacement patch has the main aim to achieve a SMBIOS iMacPro1,1<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">specific PCI implementation. Note that under SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 all other PC0x definitions remain unchanged.<br><br>
Please enable now the PC0x -&gt; PCIx ACPI DSDT replacement patch.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace [Hex]<br>
PC00 -&gt; PCI0 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;50433030 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 50434930<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div><br>
c.) SL05 -&gt; GFX0 is a graphics related ACPI DSDT replacement patch to achieve consistency with the SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 variable<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">naming. This ACPI DSDT replacement patch is not mainboard but slot specific! All mainboard users with their GPU in PCIe Slot 1 can now enable this ACPI DSDT replacement patch.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Replace [Hex]<br>
SL05 -&gt; GFX0 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;534c3035 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;47465830</div></div>All mainboard users with their GPU in a PCIe Slot different from one have to adopt the patch previously. E.g. with a GPU in PCIe Slot 4, the ACPI DSDT replacement patch looks the following.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Replace [Hex]<br>
SL01 -&gt; GFX0 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;534c3031 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;47465830</div></div>Users with two GPUs in PCIe Slot 1 and 4 might use the following ACPI DSDT replacement patches<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Replace [Hex]<br>
SL05 -&gt; GFX0 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;534c3035 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;47465830<br>
SL01 -&gt; GFX1 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;534c3031 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;47465831<br>
&nbsp;</div></div>Note that the respective ACPI DSDT replacement patch(es) are not GPU brand specific.<br><br>
However, the SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml, which will be addressed in detail in Section E.9.2) below, can have GPU brand dependent device definitions and can also be sensitive with respect to the GPU PCIe population.​</div><br>
d.) XHCI -&gt; XHC1 is a USB related ACPI DSDT replacement patch to achieve consistency with the SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 variable<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">naming. This ACPI DSDT replacement patch is not mainboard, build or PCIe slot population specific.<br><br>
Thus, all users can now enable the XHCI -&gt; XHC1 ACPI DSDT replacement patch.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Replace [Hex]<br>
XHCI -&gt; XHC1 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;58484349 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;58484331</div></div></div><br>
e.) OSI -&gt; XOSI, EC0_ -&gt; EC__ and H_EC  -&gt; EC__ are once more ACPI DSDT replacement patches to achieve consistency with<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">the SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 variable naming.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">i.) XOSI functionality is required as explained by <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/429483/" class="" target="_blank">@RehabMan</a> (just follow this <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/threads/guide-10-11-usb-changes-and-solutions.173616/" class="internalLink">LINK</a> for further<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">details).<br><br>
The ACPI code can use the_OSI method (implemented by the ACPI host) to check which Windows version is running. Most DSDT implementations will vary the USB configuration depending on the active Windows version. When running OS X, none of the DSDT _OSI("Windows &lt;version&gt;") checks will return "true" as there is only response from "Darwin". This issue can be solved by implementing the "OS Check Fix" family of DSDT patches in the SSDT-X299.aml. By DSDT patching we can simulate a certain version of Windows although running Darwin and we can obtain a system behaviour similar to a windows version specific environment. The respective SSDT-X299.aml implementations will be discussed in Section E.10.2) below. Note that in addition to the OSI -&gt; XOSI DSDT Replacement Patch, one needs to add the<br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssdt-xosi-aml-zip.294508/?temp_hash=39c342aa1f08de6a9535787159d62276" class="internalLink">SSDT-XOSI.aml</a> in the /EFI/Clover/ACPI/pathed directory of the System Disk EFI-Folder.<br>
​</div>ii.) On the Asus X299 Prime Deluxe and most likely on all other X299 mobos we have the EC0 and H_EC controllers, which<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">have to be renamed to 'EC' for proper USB power management.  Thus once more investigate your mainboard specific IOREG entry and enable both EC0_ -&gt; EC__ or and H_EC  -&gt; EC__ DSDT Replacement Patches.<br>
​</div><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Replace [Hex]<br>
OSI -&gt; XOSI &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;5f4f5349 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;584f5349<br>
EC0_ -&gt; EC__ &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 4543305f &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;45435f5f<br>
H_EC &nbsp;-&gt; EC__ &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;485f4543 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;45435f5f<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div>f.) GBE1 -&gt; ETH0 and D0A4  -&gt; ETH1 are ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe specific LAN related ACPI DSDT replacement patches<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">to achieve consistency with the SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 variable naming. All ASUS Prime X299 users can now enable the respective ACPI DSDT replacement patches. Note that the XGBE and ETH1 implementations in the SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml addressed in Section E.9.2.) are of cosmetic nature. All users of mainboards different from the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe have to find their mainboard-specific LAN-entries in the IOREG and replace the "GBE1" and "D0A4" ACPI DSDT Replacement Patches and SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml implementations depending on the mainboard in use. Alternatively, the GBE1 -&gt; XGBE and D0A4  -&gt; ETH1 ACPI DSDT replacement patches can als maintain disabled.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace [Hex]<br>
GBE1 -&gt; XGBE &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;47424531 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 58474245<br>
D0A4 &nbsp;-&gt; ETH1 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;44304134 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 45544831<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div><br>
g.) The HEC1 -&gt; IMEI and IDER-&gt;MEID ACPI DSDT Replacement patches are Intel Management Engine Interface related and are<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">vital as MacOS requires the variable names "IMEI" and "MEID" to load the 'AppleIntelMEIDriver'. The latter functionality solves the 'iTunes/Apple Store Content Access Problem' which is discussed <a href="https://pikeralpha.wordpress.com/2016/03/24/os-x-10-11-4-wants-imei-not-heci/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fpikeralpha.wordpress.com%2F2016%2F03%2F24%2Fos-x-10-11-4-wants-imei-not-heci%2F&amp;hash=6ef31d9dbfe5419685152db71369dc7d" rel="nofollow">here</a>.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Please enable now both ACPI DSDT Replacement patches independent from your mainboard.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace [Hex]<br>
HEC1 -&gt; IMEI &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 48454331 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 494d4549<br>
IDER-&gt;MEID &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;49444552 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 4d454944<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div><br>
h.)  The PMC1 -&gt; PMCR ACPI DSDT patch replacement is Power Management Controller (PMC) related and applied for consistency<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">with the PMC naming on real Macs.<br><br>
Please enable now this ACPI DSDT replacement patch independent from your mainboard.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Replace [Hex]<br>
PMC1 -&gt; PMCR &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 504d4331 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;504d4352<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div>i.) The LPC0 -&gt; LPCB ACPI DSDT Replacement Patch is AppleLPC and SMBus related and is applied for consistency with the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">variable naming on a real Mac. Note that LPCB injects AppleLPC, which however is not required in the X299 environment. X299 Systems seem to have sleep problems with the SMBus properties injected. Thus, the LPCB functionality will be disabled within the SSDT-X299.aml.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Please enable now this ACPI DSDT replacement patch independent from your mainboard.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace [Hex]<br>
LPC0 -&gt; LPCB &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 4c504330 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 4c504342<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div><br>
j.) FPU_-&gt;MATH, TMR_-&gt;TIMR, PIC_-&gt;IPIC are all ACPI DSDT Replacement Patches for consistency with the variable naming<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">on a real Mac. The variables are however functionless on either our X299 boards or real Macs.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Please enable now all three ACPI DSDT Replacement Patches independent from your mainboard.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;Replace [Hex]<br>
FPU_ -&gt; MATH &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 4650555f &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;4d415448<br>
TMR_ -&gt; TIMR &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 544d525f &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;54494d52<br>
PIC_ -&gt; IPIC &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 5049435f &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;49504943<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div><br>
k.)  SLOC -&gt; ARPT is an Airport related ACPI DSDT replacement patch, which I additionally introduced for consistency with the<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">variable naming on a real Mac when using an OSX WIFI Broadcom BCM94360CD 802.11 a/b/g/n/ac + Bluetooth 4.0 PCIe Adapter on the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe in PCIe Slot 3. The respective SSDT-X299.aml implementations will be addressed in Section E.9.2).<br><br>
All ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe and OSX WIFI Broadcom BCM94360CD 802.11 a/b/g/n/ac + Bluetooth 4.0 users with the PCIe Adapter in PCIe Slot 3 can now enable the respective ACPI DSDT Replacement patch.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace [Hex]<br>
SLOC -&gt; ARPT &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 534c3043 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 41525054<br>
&nbsp;</div></div>All OSX WIFI Broadcom BCM94360CD 802.11 a/b/g/n/ac + Bluetooth 4.0 users of different mainboards or with the PCIe Adapter in a PCIe Slot different from 3 have to primarily verify and likely adopt/modify the SLOC -&gt; ARPT in concordance with the IOREG entries for their specific mainboard and build or slot population. Users without the OSX WIFI Broadcom BCM94360CD 802.11 a/b/g/n/ac + Bluetooth 4.0 PCIe Adapter can simply leave this ACPI DSDT replacement patch disabled. Users of a WIFI and Bluetooth Adapter different from the OSX WIFI Broadcom BCM94360CD 802.11 a/b/g/n/ac + Bluetooth 4.0 can enable this ACPI DSDT replacement patch but might have to adopt the SSDT-X299-iMacPro device implementation discussed in Section E9.2 below.​</div><br><br>
l.) SL01 -&gt; UPSB is a Thunderbolt related  ACPI DSDT replacement patch for consistency with the variable<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">naming on a real Mac when using the ASUS TBEX 3 PCIe Adapter on the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe in PCIe Slot 4. All respective users can now enable this ACPI DSDT replacement patch.<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace [Hex]<br>
SL01 -&gt; UPSB &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 534c3031 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 55505342<br>
&nbsp;</div></div>ASUS mainboard users with the TBEX 3 in a PCIe slot different from 4 have to primarily adopt the ACPI DSDT replacement patch in concordance with the IOREG entries for their specific mainboard and slot population. Users without the ASUS TBEX 3 or any other TB PCIe Adapter can simply leave this ACPI DSDT replacement patch disabled. Users of a TB Adapter different from the ASUS TBEX 3 can enable this ACPI DSDT replacement patch but might have to adopt the SSDT-X299-iMacPro device implementation discussed in Section E9.2 below.​</div><br>
m.) The DSM -&gt; XDSM DSDT replacement patch is vital for loading the SSDT-X299.aml, as all DSM methods used in the original<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">DSDT do have a not compatible structure totally different from the real Mac environment. Without any fix, all DSM methods would be simply ignored. Note that one single device can have only one DSM method, which can assign additional properties to the respective device.​</div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Thus please enable the latter DSDT replacement patch completely independent from your mainboard!<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Comment: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Find*[Hex] &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Replace [Hex]<br>
_DSM -&gt; XDSM &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; 5f44534d &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;5844534d<br>
&nbsp;</div></div></div><br><br><b>E.9.2)  SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml PCI Implementation</b><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/pci-device-implementation-png.304026/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/pci-device-implementation-png.304026/" alt="PCI-Device-Implementation.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
For the proper PCI device implementation (detailed in the Figure above), which is mostly of cosmetic nature and not always directly related to device functionality, we now have to revise and likely adopt or modify the attached <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/ssdt-x299-imacpro-aml-zip.304028/?temp_hash=d856860230e0446e324db4e2364083ec" class="internalLink">SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml</a> to our specific build and system configuration with the help of the IORegistryExplorer. The entire section can also be simply skipped by unexperienced users, who also prefer to skip the implementation of the SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml and respective PCI Device implementation.<br><br>
Note that for each device, the SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml contains a DefinitionBlock entry and the underlying PCI device implementation. In case of necessary modifications/adaptations, don't forget to also modify/adapt the respective DefinitionBlock entries in concordance with your IOREG entries. The entire SSDT structure is module like. Each module can be independently added, changed or removed in dependence of your specific build, needs and requirements. A stepwise implementation of the individual PCI devices is recommended!<br><br><b>E.9.2.1) - HDEF - onboard PCI Audio Controller PCI Implementation:</b><br><br><span style="text-decoration: underline">DefintionBlock entry:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">External (_SB_.PCI0.HDEF, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)</div></div><span style="text-decoration: underline">PCI Device Implementation:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
Scope (\_SB.PCI0.HDEF)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Method (_DSM, 4, NotSerialized) &nbsp;// _DSM: Device-Specific Method<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Store (Package (0x16)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; "AAPL,slot-name",<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Buffer (0x09)<br>

&nbsp;</div></div>The HDEF PCI device implementation is valid for the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe and likely for all other mainboards with the Realtek ALC S1220A Audio Controller chipset. It is a build-in device and does not have any slot specific dependency. In any case verify device path "PCI0.HDEF" and PCI device implementations by means of IOREG.<br><br><br><b>E.9.2.2) - GFX0, HDAU - Nvidia Graphics Card and HDMI/DP Audio PCI implementation </b><br><br><span style="text-decoration: underline">DefintionBlock entry:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
External (_SB_.PC02.BR2A, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)<br>
External (_SB_.PC02.BR2A.GFX0, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)<br>
External (GFX0, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)<br>

&nbsp;</div></div>The actual GFX0 and HDAU PCI device implementation is valid for SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 (GFX0), the ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe and any Nvidia Graphics Card implemented in PCIe Slot 1.<br><br>
It is a build and PCIe slot population dependent device implementation. Nvidia Graphics Card users with more than one graphics card, or with an Nvidia graphics card in a PCIe slot different from PCIe Slot 1, will have to adopt the respective device path entries PC02.BR2A, PCIe Slot definitions and PCI device properties following their respective IOREG entries.<br><br>
Below one finds an example of <a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/members/190386/" class="" target="_blank">@apfelnico</a> for a GFX and HDAU PCI implementation of 2x Radeon Vega 64 in PCIe Slot 1 and 4. Note that for such implementation also requires an additional DSDT Replacement patch, namely:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">SL01-&gt;GFX1 &nbsp; &nbsp; 534c3031 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;47465831 </div></div><span style="text-decoration: underline">DefintionBlock entry:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; External (_SB_.PC02.BR2A, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; External (_SB_.PC02.BR2A.SL05, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; External (_SB_.PC01.BR1A, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; External (_SB_.PC01.BR1A.SL01, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)<br>
&nbsp;</div></div><span style="text-decoration: underline">PCI Device Implementation:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>

&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; }<br><br>
&nbsp;</div></div>Note that the XGBE/ETH1 Intel I219V2 PCI Express Gigabit Ethernet and Intel I211VA PCI Express Gigabit Ethernet onboard LAN controller PCI implementations are of pure cosmetic nature and only valid for ASUS Prime X299 Deluxe or X299 mainboards with the same LAN Controller configuration. Owners of different X299 mainboards have to verify and adopt/modify if necessary the device these PCI device implementations by means of IOREG.<br><br><b><span style="text-decoration: underline">E.9.2.12) - ARPT - OSX WIFI Broadcom BCM94360CD 802.11 a/b/g/n/ac + Bluetooth 4.0 AirPort Controller PCI Implementation:</span></b><br><br><span style="text-decoration: underline">DefintionBlock entry:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">External (_SB_.PC03.BR3D.ARPT, DeviceObj) &nbsp; &nbsp;// (from opcode)</div></div><span style="text-decoration: underline">PCI Device Implementation:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>

&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>

&nbsp;</div></div>The ARPT OSX WIFI Broadcom BCM94360CD 802.11 a/b/g/n/ac + Bluetooth 4.0 AirPort Controller PCI device implementation is of pure cosmetic nature and only valid for users of the latter WIFI/Bluetooth PCIe Adapter in PCIe Slot 3. Users of this PCIe Adapter within a PCIe slot population different from PCIe Slot 3 have to adapt/modify the respective device path "PC03.BR3D.ARPT" and likely also the respective ACPI DSDT Replacement Patch. Users of the Asus Prime X299 Deluxe onboard Bluetooth chipset controller or with a completely different WIFI/Bluetooth configuration have to either adopt the entire Airport PCI implementation by means of IOREG or can also skip the entire part.<br><br><b><span style="text-decoration: underline">E.9.2.13) - ThunderboltEX 3 Controller PCI Implementation:</span></b><br><br><span style="text-decoration: underline">DefintionBlock entry:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code"><br>

&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; },<br><br>

&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;0x00 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; },<br><br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; "name",<br>

&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Return (Local0)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br><br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Method (_DSM, 4, NotSerialized) &nbsp;// _DSM: Device-Specific Method<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Store (Package (0x02)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; "PCI-Thunderbolt",<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; One<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }, Local0)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; DTGP (Arg0, Arg1, Arg2, Arg3, RefOf (Local0))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Return (Local0)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; }<br><br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; Method (DTGP, 5, NotSerialized)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; If (LEqual (Arg0, ToUUID ("a0b5b7c6-1318-441c-b0c9-fe695eaf949b")))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; If (LEqual (Arg1, One))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; If (LEqual (Arg2, Zero))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Store (Buffer (One)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;0x03 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }, Arg4)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Return (One)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br><br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; If (LEqual (Arg2, One))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Return (One)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br><br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Store (Buffer (One)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;0x00 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }, Arg4)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Return (Zero)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
}<br>
&nbsp;</div></div>The ThunderboltEX 3 PCI device implementation (in my personal opinion by far the most sophisticated and most beautiful PCI device implementation performed by @afpelnico) is of pure cosmetic nature and only valid for users of the latter TB PCIe Adapter in PCIe Slot 4. Users of this PCIe Adapter within a PCIe slot population different from PCIe Slot 3 have to adapt/modify the respective path entires "PC01", "BR1A" and likely also the respective UPSB ACPI DSDT Replacement. Users of TB PCIe Adapters different from the ASUS TBEX 3 or users without any TB PCIe Adapter, have to either adopt the entire TB PCI implementation by means of IOREG or can simply skip the entire part.<br><br>
Note that ThunderboltEX 3 PCI device implementation also performs the following ACPI Replacement:<br><br>
PC01.BR1A.UPSB.DSB2.UPS0 -&gt; PC01.BR1A.UPSB.DSB2.XHC5<br><br>
in concordance with the respective SMBIOS iMacPro1,1 variable naming.<br><br><b><span style="text-decoration: underline">E.9.2.13) - DTGP Method:</span></b><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">Method (DTGP, 5, NotSerialized)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; If (LEqual (Arg0, ToUUID ("a0b5b7c6-1318-441c-b0c9-fe695eaf949b")))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; If (LEqual (Arg1, One))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; If (LEqual (Arg2, Zero))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Store (Buffer (One)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;0x03 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }, Arg4)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Return (One)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br><br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; If (LEqual (Arg2, One))<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Return (One)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }<br><br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Store (Buffer (One)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; {<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;0x00 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; }, Arg4)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Return (Zero)<br>
&nbsp; &nbsp; }<br>
}</div></div>The DTG Method Implementation is required for SSDT functionality and has not to be modified or adopted in any case.<br><br>
After successfully implementing the ACPI DSDT Replacement Patches, SSDT-X299-iMacPro.aml and SSDT-XOSI.aml, my System possesses full sleep/wake functionality even with the ThunderboltEX 3 PCIe Adapter implemented.<br><br>
Note that in addition I added the "darkwake=1" and "nv_spanmodepolicy=1" boot flags to my config.plist by means of Clover Configurator, Section "Boot", "Arguments". "nv_spanmodepolicy=1" can be unchecked by all AMD graphics card users.<br><br><br><b><span class="size4">E.10) System Overview CPU Cosmetics</span></b><br><br>
As our Skylake-X CPU at present will not be properly recognised by OS X, Apple's System Overview ("About This Mac") reveals incomplete or simply wrong CPU details. Many times CPU's like the i9-7980XE are implemented as "unknown"...<br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/overview-png.286632/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/overview-png.286632/" alt="Overview.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
I recently discovered on InsanelyMac a <a href="http://www.insanelymac.com/forum/topic/323469-change-cpu-name-in-about-this-mac/#entry2419380" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.insanelymac.com%2Fforum%2Ftopic%2F323469-change-cpu-name-in-about-this-mac%2F%23entry2419380&amp;hash=5512361734365608985b23b12dce07d2" rel="nofollow">sophisticated fix</a> of pure cosmetic nature developed by <a href="http://www.insanelymac.com/forum/user/707419-shaneee/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.insanelymac.com%2Fforum%2Fuser%2F707419-shaneee%2F&amp;hash=b389bb284ad60312045d4b4f48ed588b" rel="nofollow">Shaneee</a> (also thanks to <a href="http://www.insanelymac.com/forum/user/468967-fabiosun/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.insanelymac.com%2Fforum%2Fuser%2F468967-fabiosun%2F&amp;hash=005ce02e877dcd406f854c8748eb3c3a" rel="nofollow">fabiosun</a> for pointing me to this direction), which allows to implement those CPU details you want to be implemented. For the sake of simplicity, I summarise below the necessary steps.<br><br>
1.) Open a terminal and use the following commands:<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">cp /System/Library/PrivateFrameworks/AppleSystemInfo.framework/Versions/A/Resources/English.lproj/AppleSystemInfo.strings ~/Desktop/</div></div><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo mv /System/Library/PrivateFrameworks/AppleSystemInfo.framework/Versions/A/Resources/English.lproj/AppleSystemInfo.strings /System/Library/PrivateFrameworks/AppleSystemInfo.framework/Versions/A/Resources/English.lproj/AppleSystemInfo.strings-Backup</div></div></div>2.) Open "AppleSystemInfo.strings" on your Desktop with <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/de/app/textwrangler/id404010395?mt=12" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fitunes.apple.com%2Fde%2Fapp%2Ftextwrangler%2Fid404010395%3Fmt%3D12&amp;hash=e0d5fea652c8e19c447c4d9d52af5aca" rel="nofollow">TextWrangler</a> and change<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">&lt;key&gt;UnknownCPUKind&lt;/key&gt;<br>
&lt;string&gt;Unknown&lt;/string&gt;</div></div>to what ever you want. In my case I choose:<br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">&lt;key&gt;UnknownCPUKind&lt;/key&gt;<br>
&lt;string&gt;4,4 GHz 18-core 36-thread Skylake-X i9-7980XE&lt;/string&gt;</div></div></div><br><div style="padding-left: 30px">Save  "AppleSystemInfo.strings"<br>
​</div>3.) Run the following terminal commands:<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo codesign -f -s - ~/Desktop/AppleSystemInfo.strings</div></div><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo cp ~/Desktop/AppleSystemInfo.strings /System/Library/PrivateFrameworks/AppleSystemInfo.framework/Versions/A/Resources/English.lproj/</div></div>and reboot your system.<br>
​</div>4.) Open your config.plist with Clover Configurator and in Section "CPU" set "Type" to "Unknown". Save the config.plist and<br><div style="padding-left: 30px">reboot.<br>
​</div>5.) Apple's System Overview now will reveal the following details:<br><br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/overview-correct-png.286655/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/overview-correct-png.286655/" alt="Overview-correct.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br>
​</div><span style="text-decoration: underline">As fall back option enter the following terminal commands:</span><br><br><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo rm /System/Library/PrivateFrameworks/AppleSystemInfo.framework/Versions/A/Resources/English.lproj/AppleSystemInfo.strings</div></div><div class="bbCodeBlock bbCodeCode"><div class="type">Code (Text):</div><div class="code">sudo mv /System/Library/PrivateFrameworks/AppleSystemInfo.framework/Versions/A/Resources/English.lproj/AppleSystemInfo.strings-Backup /System/Library/PrivateFrameworks/AppleSystemInfo.framework/Versions/A/Resources/English.lproj/AppleSystemInfo.string</div></div>and reboot.<br><div style="padding-left: 30px"><br>
​</div><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span class="size4"></span></span><span class="size4"><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">F.) Benchmarking</span></b></span><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/img_9290-jpg.294976/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/img_9290-jpg.294976/" alt="IMG_9290.jpg" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><b><span class="size4">F.1) Sylake-X Intel I9-7980XE CPU Benchmarking</span></b><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/i9-png.294709/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/i9-png.294709/" alt="i9.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/xcpm-new-png.301307/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/xcpm-new-png.301307/" alt="xcpm-new.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cpu-benchmarks-png.303988/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/cpu-benchmarks-png.303988/" alt="cpu-benchmarks.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><b><span class="size4">F.1) Gigabyte AORUS GTX 1080 Ti Waterforce EB 11GB Extreme Edition Benchmarking</span><br></b><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/img_9291-jpg.294977/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/img_9291-jpg.294977/" alt="IMG_9291.jpg" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/graphicsbench-png.303989/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/graphicsbench-png.303989/" alt="graphicsbench.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a><br><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><span class="size4"></span></span><span class="size4"><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">G.) Summary and Conclusion:</span></b></span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">Already during the individual macOS High Sierra 10.13 beta releases, Syklake-X/X299 systems reached full functionality together with flawless stability. Now it might be the right moment to follow my Desktop Guide and to unfold the unbelievable Skylake-X/X299 potential together with macOS High Sierra 10.13!</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">I am quite optimistic that high-end builds based on extremely novel Skylake-X/X299 technology will find manifold application, not only in science and research at universities or research institutions, engineering facilities, or medical labs, etc... Skylake-X processors with up to 18 cores (36 threads) and turbo frequencies up to 4.5 GHz will make make X299 to a "relatively cheap" but really serious alternative to the yet to be released iMac Pro's and Mac Pro's. The principal intention of this desktop guide was to demonstrate, that we are able to build and configure fully functional and relatively "low-cost" high-end systems nowadays, which go far beyond of what Apple is able to offer at present or will be ever able to offer for some reasonable pricing. A Skylake-X/X299-System, that allows the use of all software-packages developed for MacOS, Unix, Linux or even Windows at the same time (e.g. think on Vine, Parallels, or a dual boot system configuration). The flexibility between different mainboards (Asus, Gigabyte, ASRock, MSI, etc.), different Skylake-X processors, and different RAM memory configurations (16-128GB) should make such system affordable for anybody (also home office, audio and video editing/production, etc.) and allow its perfect adaptation for the specific purpose, requirements and available budgets. It might not be necessary to outline, that current Skylake-X/X299 Systems perform absolutely stable on a 24/7/365 basis.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">I am a scientist, expert in solar physics, space weather forecast and related telescope/instrument/space-mission development. In the frame of my scientific research, I developed parallelized image reconstruction, spectral line inversion and numerical modeling algorithms/applications, which require tremendous parallelized calculation power, RAM memory and storage capacities to reduce, analyze and interpret extensive and pioneering scientific ground-based or space-born observational data sets. This basically was also the professional motivation for my innovative Customac-Pro build iSPOR-S, the</span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"> i</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">maging </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">S</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">pectropolarimetric </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">P</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">arallel </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">O</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">rganized </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">R</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">econstruction </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">S</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">erver running iSPOR-DP, the </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">I</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">maging </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">S</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">pectropolarimetric </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">P</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">arallel </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">O</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">rganized </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">R</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">econstruction </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">D</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">ata </span><b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">P</span></b><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">ipeline software package for the GREGOR Fabry-Pérot Interferometer, located at the 1.5m GREGOR Solar Telescope (Europe's largest solar telescope) on Tenerife, Canary Islands, Spain. Anybody interested can find more details on my </span><a href="https://www.klaus-gerhard-puschmann.de/" target="_blank" class="externalLink ProxyLink" data-proxy-href="proxy.php?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.klaus-gerhard-puschmann.de%2F&amp;hash=7ef56a0ff6a849011439c98ca7b6d75a" rel="nofollow">personal webpage</a><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)">.</span><br><br><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0)"><a href="https://www.tonymacx86.com/attachments/avatar4-png.272069/" target="_blank" class="LbTrigger" data-href="misc/lightbox"><img src="data/attachments/226/226978-89339c6ea4564c8b266fe5193bdd64af.jpg" alt="avatar4.png" class="bbCodeImage LbImage"></a></span><div class="messageTextEndMarker">&nbsp;</div></blockquote></article></div></div><div id="likes-post-1561329" class="messageLikes"><div class="likesSummary secondaryContent"><span class="LikeText"><a href="members/classicmartini.1560886/" class="username" dir="auto">ClassicMartini</a>, <a href="members/greend.1324417/" class="username" dir="auto">Greend</a>, <a href="members/thireus.22313/" class="username" dir="auto">Thireus</a> and <a href="posts/1561329/likes" class="OverlayTrigger">39 others</a> like this.
